They also telegraphed the Central Government, the original text of which read: To the Central Executive Committee: Just after the telegram to Guangdong was sent this morning, we suddenly received definite news that Japanese troops actually occupied the Shenyang-Yingkou area this morning and are showing signs of advancing. We have neither provoked nor resisted in any way. The country is in imminent danger, and it is imperative to jointly resist foreign aggression. We urge comrades in Guangdong and Guangxi to immediately announce the elimination of hostile situations and unite to save the nation. We earnestly hope and pray for it. Yu Ying, Ji Tiecheng, and Kou Hao, etc., respectfully report. Yu Ying, Ji Tiecheng, and Kou Hao, etc., salute. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Central Government has never given up its advocacy of peace regarding the Guangdong Mutiny, patiently enduring and waiting for enlightenment. After receiving the news of the Japanese invasion and occupation of Shenyang, it believed that the national crisis was even more urgent and that there was no way to unite against foreign aggression without realizing peaceful unification. In addition to Chairman Chiang's previous telegram inviting members Zhang and Li to come south to discuss the peace movement together, the Central Government plans to telegraph Guangdong again, earnestly advising them to unite the country to resist foreign aggression. (19th Special Dispatch)

Reasons for the Japanese Advance 39

Observations from the Foreign Perspective

(Tianjin) Observers who have been paying attention to the long-term preparations of the Japanese army have known for several months that there would inevitably be a break between China and Japan one day, but they did not know when or how it would break. Now they know. Japan has occupied Shenyang, Kuanchengtzu (the important intersection of the South Manchuria, Central Eastern, and Jichang railway lines), Niuzhuang, and Goubangzi (Beining Railway). It has also sent troops to land in Qingdao. During the Japanese army's extremely well-arranged and well-commanded actions, many Chinese were killed or injured. According to Japanese news, only one Japanese officer was injured and one soldier was killed. According to the Japanese, the most recent cause of this strong action by the Japanese was the incident on Friday night at 10:30 p.m. when Chinese soldiers from Beida Camp blew up a section of the South Manchuria Railway. However, this has not been confirmed by the Chinese side and is difficult to verify, as the section has already been repaired and is operating as usual. At the same time, Beida Camp has been occupied, and several Chinese soldiers were killed or injured in the shelling and later disarmed. Upon investigation, an accessory reason that aided the Japanese action was, of course, the spread of a certain piece of news. It is said that Rong Zhen, Chief of Staff of the Northeast Army, has confirmed that Nakamura and three companions were murdered in Inner Mongolia in June. The Japanese have been deeply stimulated by Nakamura's murder. The Japanese military has not hesitated to distribute pamphlets with inflammatory language by plane to arouse the emotions of the Japanese people. Therefore, the initial report of the Shenyang battle can be said to have originated from the Japanese soldiers venting their anger. This is what Japanese civil officials call beyond their authority. But the real reason is not here. It is heard that there are over 300 unresolved issues between China and Japan. Powerful politicians in Japan have recently held a belief that if they do not adopt harsh measures, China will continue its delaying tactics. Even members of the Minsei Party have differing opinions on whether it is appropriate for Japan to continue its mild policy towards China. Under the guidance of Minister of the Army Minami and other military personnel, Japanese emotions have become increasingly激昂 and the call for war is resounding. Japanese radicals even say that if Russia does not wage war against China, the Moscow conference will not be held and the Sino-Russian issues will not be discussed. Therefore, Japan should emulate and adopt more practical policies. This is the real reason for the Japanese military action. The Chinese side says that the Japanese are actually trying to achieve the goal of annexing Manchuria through this incident. The development of Chinese railways in Manchuria, which run parallel to the South Manchuria Railway, is clearly a great concern to Japan. The Chinese routes have lower taxes and reduced fees, which have the potential to crowd out the South Manchuria Railway and its branches. Furthermore, the discrimination against the Port of Dalian and the increased taxes on Fushun coal have also made the Japanese restless. Therefore, the Japanese are now using extreme methods to show their hand. However, the Chinese have not resisted with force, according to Zhang Xueliang's instructions. (19th Reuters Dispatch)

(Beiping) The foreign community here believes that the Japanese military authorities intend to occupy and defend Shenyang and the entire South Manchuria in order to force China to resolve the Nakamura Incident and other outstanding issues between China and Japan according to its terms. (19th Reuters Dispatch)

The Japanese Government's Attitude 40

Verbally Acknowledging it as an Unfortunate Incident

(Nanjing) The Japanese Consulate in Beijing formally notified the Ministry of Foreign Affairs that the Japanese government in Tokyo stated that it considers the Japanese military action to be an unfortunate incident and has urgently telegraphed the Japanese military in the Northeast to do its utmost to stop its actions and prevent them from expanding. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Tokyo) After the Manchurian Incident occurred, stock market prices fell. However, it is heard that the Governor of the Bank of Japan said that this matter will not greatly affect business. Textile manufacturers are concerned about the sluggish sales of cotton goods to China and fear that Japanese-owned textile factories in Shanghai and Qingdao may be forced to shut down as a result. The British Ambassador and diplomatic representatives from several other countries visited the Ministry of Foreign Affairs today to inquire about the details of the Shenyang Incident. The Foreign Minister told reporters that he regretted the occurrence of this incident and explained the necessity of preventing the incident from expanding. In the afternoon, the Minister of the Army told reporters that the situation was gradually calming down and that there was no need to send reinforcements from Korea unless there were unexpected developments. The Army Ministry said that several aircraft have been dispatched from the Pyongyang Air Force to Shenyang to inspect the situation there and maintain communication between the Kwantung and Korean armies. According to the latest news telegrams obtained in Tokyo, the situation is indeed gradually calming down. (19th Reuters Dispatch)

⊙Osaka The news of the Shenyang military action caused stock market prices to plummet when the market opened here this morning. The prices of commodities also fell for the same reason. (19th Reuters Dispatch)

(Tokyo) After the Shenyang Incident occurred, Minister of the Army Minami immediately held emergency discussions with Chief of the General Staff Kanaya and Director-General of Education Muto to establish countermeasures. Minister of the Army Minami then attended the Provisional Cabinet Meeting. It is heard that the future countermeasures are as follows: If the Kwantung Army cannot resolve the situation, the first step will be at the discretion of Commander Hayashi to dispatch an appropriate number of troops from the Korean Division. If that is still not enough, it has been decided to send reinforcements from Japan proper. In addition to telegraphing this decision to Commander Hayashi of the Korean Army, he is also estimating the budget and preparing everything. (19th Den Tsushinsha Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Navy authorities held an emergency meeting this morning, attended by top officials including Minister of the Navy Anbo, to discuss the Navy's attitude towards the situation. As a result, in case the incident expands, and to prevent the danger to the lives and property of Japanese residents in various parts of Manchuria, the Second Overseas Fleet in Qingdao and the destroyers stationed in Lushun, such as Kayari, Asagao, and Fuyo, were ordered to take on special security duties. If the situation becomes urgent, the 24th Destroyer Squadron will be dispatched from Sasebo. (19th Den Tsushinsha Dispatch)

⊙Andong Colonel Doihara, who had been recalled to Japan by the Japanese government and was currently returning to his post, arrived in Andong today. Regarding the firing between the two armies, he said that such a thing is a matter of course. At this time, Japan's vested interests in Manchuria and Mongolia must be thoroughly resolved. If a third country comes out to arbitrate, it should be resolutely rejected. (19th Den Tsushinsha Dispatch)

Tianjin Party and Government Joint Meeting 41

(Tianjin) The Tianjin Municipal Party Headquarters convened a joint party and government meeting at 3:00 p.m. on the 19th. More than 100 representatives from various agencies attended. Chairman Liu Chenzhang of the Reorganization Committee reported that the Japanese army's occupation of our three eastern provinces was a planned action. Our military and civilians should unite in anger and work hard against Japan. The following four proposals were then passed: (1) Telegraph the Guangdong government to urge them to awaken and unite against foreign aggression. (2) Announce the situation of the Japanese army's forcible occupation of Shenyang and other places to the public. (3) Publicize the Japanese army's atrocities to the international community in order to seek fairness. (4) Starting immediately, the entire city will lower flags to half-mast for three days to mourn the deceased compatriots. (19th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Residents in Harbin Seek Protection 42

(Harbin) The Deputy Consul of the Japanese Consulate in Harbin, Nakano, visited the garrison commander Ding Chao and police chief Wang Ruihua today, along with infantryman Zhong Yu,

Page 12

requesting the protection of Japanese residents. The various officials promised to provide practical protection. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Harbin) The Railway Protection Army Headquarters dispatched staff member Yang to Changchun this afternoon to investigate the truth. The Harbin Japanese Consulate dispatched personnel to Garrison Commander Ding Chao, negotiator Zhong Yu, and Special Police Chief Wang Ruihua this morning to request the protection of Japanese residents. The various officials promised to do their best. (19th Special Dispatch)

Yu Hanmou's Troops Return to Guangdong 43

Troops Attacking Hunan and Guangdong-Guangxi All Withdraw

(Hong Kong) Yu Hanmou returned to Lechang from Hunan on the 16th and returned to Shaozhou and then to the province on the 17th. Yu's troops returned to Pingshi and Lechang on the 17th and were being transported to the province in succession, expected to arrive completely around the 21st or 22nd. Li Yangjing's troops started on the 14th and returned from Laiyang, still stationed in Shaozhou. Tang Shengzhi returned to Yizhang on the 16th, expected to arrive in Shaozhou around the 20th. Li Zhenqiu arrived in the province on the 18th, on the orders of Yu Hanmou. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Chen Jitang plans to set up a field headquarters in Huiyang, appointing Du Yiqian as director. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Tang Shaoyi arrived in the province from his hometown on the 18th. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) He Chengjun stated that the vanguard mixed troops of Guangdong and Guangxi attacking Hunan reached three miles south of Hengzhou on the 12th. Just as they were preparing to cross the river, they were defeated by the stationed troops, and then the entire army retreated. The Guangxi troops still fled back to Huangsha River and Quanzhou, and the Guangdong troops fled back to Yizhang and Pingshi. According to reports yesterday, they are still continuing to retreat, which proves that the internal strife in Guangdong and Guangxi is about to erupt, and it also shows that those who betray the Central Government will inevitably fail. (19th Special Dispatch)

The Yangtze River Continues to Recede in Hankou 44

(Hankou) The river receded a total of seven inches on the 18th and 19th. The water level is 48 feet and 9 inches. It is heard that drainage will be implemented once the water recedes another foot. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) The Relief Sub-Committee ordered 100,000 sets of cotton clothing from the Wuchang Clothing Factory on the 19th, requiring approximately 240,000 yuan. A contract will be signed once the funds from the General Committee arrive. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) The Emergency Relief Association ordered Hanyang to prohibit the slaughter of draft cattle and sealed up the various cattle slaughterhouses. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) He Chengjun inspected the temporary hospital on the 19th. (19th Special Dispatch)

Matters Regarding Flood Prevention and Disaster Relief 45

(Nanjing) Li Yizhi, President of the Chinese Hydraulic Engineering Society, and Li Shutian, Vice President, suggested to the National Government to establish a central supreme authority to exclusively manage water affairs in order to unify national water administration. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance announced that the first tranche of disaster relief bonds, worth 30 million yuan, has already begun to be issued in Shanghai and is expected to be fully subscribed within one or two weeks. The contract for the loan of American wheat has been drafted in accordance with the principles decided by the Central Political Council and will be signed by both parties. The representatives signing on our side will be the Chairman of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee and the Minister of Foreign Affairs. The U.S. representatives will be the U.S. Consul General in Beijing and the Ministers of Agriculture and Foreign Affairs. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industry and Commerce telegraphed the Flood Relief Committee, requesting that 20,000 dan of American wheat be allocated first when it arrives in China, to be distributed to various places to exchange for suitable seeds to remedy winter crops. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Capital Flood Relief Association requested an allocation of 3,000 yuan for epidemic prevention expenses. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Capital City Educational Institutions Flood Donation Committee has decided to hold a donation and entertainment event for three days starting on the 26th, planning to raise 5,000 yuan to assist with disaster relief. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Jilin) The Provincial Government, following Zhang Xueliang's instructions, formed the Jilin Branch of the Northeast Disaster Relief Committee. A meeting was held today, attended by the leaders of all organs and legal entities in the city, to discuss the progress of the work. It was decided to appoint Zhang Songling, Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, and Yan Aichen, Director of the Official Silver Bureau, as the General and Deputy Directors, respectively, and the heads of various departments, offices, bureaus, and institutions as directors. The Finance Department will immediately allocate funds, and the Official Silver Bureau will purchase 7,000 shi of relief grain and transport it to Yingkou for shipment south, while also actively raising funds and purchasing grain as much as possible. (19th Special Dispatch)

He Chengjun Discusses Progress in Disaster Relief 46

(Hankou) He Chengjun stated that disaster relief in Wuhan is progressing and that he is starting disaster relief in various counties, first by implementing price controls to maintain the people's food supply. The post-disaster public bonds are still being negotiated by Wu Guozhen in Beijing and Shanghai, with the salt tax or business tax being used as collateral. As for the dredging of the river, he will request the Central Government to plan and implement the project to open up tributaries of the Xiang River, and the local government will handle the repair of Hankou's roads. Surveying will begin after the water recedes. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) He Chengjun decided to request the Central Government to issue New Wuhan Construction and Industrial Relief Bonds worth 20 million yuan to finance the reconstruction of Wuhan, guaranteed by Wuhan's land tax, or to allow the borrowing of foreign debts of 20 million yuan, to be repaid over ten years. (19th Special Dispatch)

Liu's Remnants Flee Toward Rizhao

(Jinan) Han returned to Jinan on the evening of the 18th and told me that the situation in Jiaodong, which he had inspected, was still good. However, Liu Guitang and Guo Maofeng were causing trouble in Juxian, Yishui, and Linyi. He has dispatched Zhan Shutang's and Qiao Lizhi's two divisions and the pistol brigade to Zaozhuang to suppress them. Zhang Heilian is also蠢動ing in Baodu Mountain. He must be thoroughly suppressed as he was in the spring. I am confident in suppressing the bandits. Once all the armies arrive, I will go to Zaozhuang to supervise the army. Juxian and Linyi have already been relieved. Han has been giving speeches to the people of various counties for days, and his voice is hoarse. Ma Hongkui will come to Jinan to bid farewell to Han. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) Qiao Lizhi, commander of the 74th Division, took a special train to Zaozhuang today to supervise the army's suppression of the bandits. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) Liu Guitang is fleeing towards the coastal area of Rizhao southeast of Juxian. Han has decided to go to Zaozhuang on the 20th to supervise the army's suppression of the bandits. (19th Special Dispatch)

Jiangyuan Warship Runs Aground 48

(Nanjing) The Navy's Jiangyuan warship ran aground while suppressing bandits in the Xinghua area. The Yongji and Yongxu warships went to tow it to safety and will soon tow it to the Jiangnan Shipyard in Shanghai for repairs. (19th Special Dispatch)

Mr. and Mrs. Lin Bai Arrive in Beijing 49

(Nanjing) Mr. and Mrs. Lin Bai flew to Beijing from Japan on the morning of the 19th. Foreign Minister Wang, Director of the Aviation Administration Huang Bingheng, Deputy Director Cao Baoqing, the U.S. Consul, representatives from various agencies, and more than 6,000 people all went to Xiaguan to welcome them. However, the wind and waves on the river were strong, and the Lins landed on Xuanwu Lake. The welcoming personnel rushed to greet them. Foreign Minister Wang, the U.S. Consul, and Huang Chenghang stepped forward to shake hands. Miss Li Jinlun, daughter of the Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, presented flowers to show her welcome. The Lins, accompanied by the U.S. Consul, took a car to the Consulate to rest in the midst of the crowd. Various agencies in Beijing have decided to hold a welcoming ceremony on the 21st to congratulate Mr. and Mrs. Lin on completing their feat of crossing the Pacific Ocean. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Mr. and Mrs. Lin Bai are scheduled to have an audience with the Chairman of the National Government on the morning of the 21st, after the National Government's memorial week, accompanied by Huang Bingheng, Director of the Aviation Administration. At that time, the National Government will award them medals. (19th Special Dispatch)

Foreign Important Telegrams

British Tariffs Will Adopt a Protectionist System 57

Lyons Silk Industry Greatly Panicked

London Elementary School Teachers Oppose Salary Cuts

Paris Telegram from the National Assembly on the 18th. France's foreign trade deficit in August was enormous, causing great panic in political circles. In addition, with Britain on the verge of becoming a protectionist tariff country, public sentiment is even more volatile. It is heard that the government will reopen trade agreement negotiations with Soviet Russia in order to remedy the situation. The negotiations have been mostly suspended because Soviet Russia advocated long-term credit. Furthermore, the talks between the heads of government of France and Germany in Berlin in the near future seem to focus on economic issues, with the hope of reaching a close economic understanding between the two countries. Representatives of employers and workers in the Lyons silk industry came to Paris today, expressing concern about the possibility of Britain implementing protectionist taxes, saying that if it becomes a reality, the Lyons silk industry will be completely destroyed.

London Telegram from Reuters on the 18th. Tonight, 10,000 elementary school teachers held a citizens' assembly in Westminster to oppose salary cuts. Richard Lycett, Independent Member of Parliament for London University, said that reducing teachers' salaries is not only unfair, but the position of teachers can only be preserved in theory, not by rioting. Elementary school teachers' salaries must be reduced by 15 percent in accordance with the government's spending cut plan. The day after the Chancellor of the Exchequer announced it, elementary school teachers rallied and marched in London to show their protest. It is now learned that elementary school teachers have spent no less than 10,000 pounds on publicity this week to gain public support for their movement.

French-Italian Naval Negotiations Reopen 58

Geneva Telegram from the National Assembly on the 18th. French-Italian naval negotiations formally reopened here today, based on France's recently proposed memorandum as the basis for negotiations. Mr. Klegg, a naval expert from the British Foreign Office, also attended. Mr. Klegg occupied a key position at the naval conference at the beginning of the year and has now come to Geneva to continue his participation. Mr. Klegg believes that the French memorandum has an unfavorable impact on the British ratio, and Italy also opposes the main part of the memorandum, so he believes that these negotiations are unlikely to have good results.

Page 13

Foreign Important Telegrams 2

National League Special Committee Discusses Protectionist Tariffs 59

League Charter and Kellogg-Briand Pact

Still Unable to Find a Harmonious Approach

Geneva, 18th Dispatch: The Economic Committee of the League of Nations discussed the issue of protectionist tariffs today. Representatives spoke one after another, unanimously criticizing them. Swiss representative Stucki and Dutch representative Colijn spared no effort in opposing protectionism. Italian representative Buti, the Italian Finance Minister, and British representative Salter expressed skepticism regarding the proposal by French representative Rollin, the French Finance Minister, yesterday to organize an international industrial alliance and implement preferential tax rates. Finally, Denmark, Norway, Finland, Belgium, the Netherlands, Switzerland, and Luxembourg jointly moved to request that all countries in the world maintain their current tariff policies, as these are sufficient to shake economic stability. It is scheduled to continue the discussion tomorrow.

Geneva, 18th Dispatch: The First Committee of the League of Nations declared today that it has still been unable to find a way to harmonize the League of Nations Charter with the Kellogg-Briand Pact. It has now decided to form another committee to study the issue for another year.

Commentary

Overview of Japanese Military Preparations (I) 60

The Japanese have now launched an undeclared war against us. Japanese troops stationed in Korea and the Kwantung Leased Territory, as well as the Japanese air force in Pyongyang, have been urgently mobilized. Our Shenyang has been occupied. The situation is extremely serious. The Japanese plan to implement armed aggression against us is no longer a matter of a single day. From increasing troops in Korea to transferring the Governor-General of Korea, and up to the recent increase of troops in our Northeast, their prior active preparations are clearly visible. Their slogans for implementing armed aggression against us are, first, to maintain their vested interests in our Northeast, and second, to consolidate national defense. The so-called consolidation of national defense, in other words, is a disguised declaration of war against the United States and the Soviet Union. The Japanese have long regarded the United States and the Soviet Union as their hypothetical enemies, and a war will eventually be unavoidable. Since the Japanese possess such ambitions, what is their actual strength? This is what the people of our country urgently want to understand. Here, we have compiled the following overview of their military preparations and the troops stationed in our Northeast, based on what is recorded in books and newspapers. Information about the Japanese Navy, Air Force, and the military preparations of the Soviet Union and the United States will be published in future installments. This is so that the people of our country can understand the truth and promptly take emergency countermeasures.

Current Strength of the Japanese Army 61

The current strength of the Japanese Army is estimated to be 15,540 officers and 205,300 non-commissioned officers and below, totaling over 228,400 personnel. If classified by branch and company, there are 70 infantry regiments and 4 battalions, totaling 722 companies; 25 cavalry regiments, totaling 70 companies; 19 field artillery and mountain artillery regiments and 2 battalions, totaling 114 companies; 11 heavy artillery regiments (including field heavy artillery and fortress heavy artillery) and 8 battalions, totaling 78 companies; 17 engineer battalions, totaling 48 companies; 4 signal and railway regiments, totaling 32 companies; 15 transport battalions, totaling 30 companies; 8 aviation regiments and 1 battalion (balloon squadron), totaling 26 companies (currently being reorganized and expanded); 1 regiment and 1 company of tank and anti-aircraft artillery units, totaling 5 companies; for a grand total of 1,125 companies.

Japanese Military Preparations Stationed in Our Northeast 63

After the Russo-Japanese War, the Treaty of Peace of September 1905 (Meiji 38) and the Sino-Japanese Agreement of December of the same year were concluded. Based on the treaty, Japan and Russia each stationed no more than 15 soldiers per kilometer along the Chinese Eastern Railway and South Manchuria Railway lines for defense. Therefore, after the Russo-Japanese War, Japan regularly stationed two field divisions in the Northeast. In 1906 (Showa 39), the Railway Guard Unit was also formed to be responsible for guarding the railway. As a result, the Japanese troops stationed in the Northeast consisted of the division (also known as the Manchuria Garrison Army) and the independent guard unit. In addition, the Japanese troops directly guarding the Kwantung Leased Territory included the Lushun Fortress Headquarters and the heavy artillery battalion, totaling over 13,000 regular troops and over 6,000 guard troops, for a total of about 20,000 personnel.

I. Land Military Preparations

The highest-level organization for the Japanese troops stationed in the Northeast is the Kwantung Army Headquarters. The stationed troops, military organizations, include the Lushun Fortress Headquarters, the stationed division, the independent guard unit, the Lushun heavy artillery unit, and the Kwantung Military Police, army warehouses, garrison hospitals, etc. In addition, the Army Transportation Department has an office in Dalian (surveyed on September 1, 1930).

Kwantung Army Headquarters Initially, the Army Department was established within the Kwantung Government-General. The Governor-General was a general (or lieutenant general), specially appointed, and was the head of civil and military affairs in the Kwantung Leased Territory. In April of the 8th year of the Republic of China (Taisho 8), the government-general system was abolished, and the Kwantung Agency and the Kwantung Army Headquarters were established separately to administer civil and military affairs. The commander of the Kwantung Army was a general (or lieutenant general), specially appointed, directly under the Emperor, commanding the various Japanese Imperial Army units in the Northeast and the Kwantung Leased Territory, and responsible for the defense of the Kwantung Leased Territory and the South Manchuria Railway lines. The Army Headquarters had departments such as the General Staff, Adjutant's Office, Ordnance Department, Quartermaster Department, Medical Department, Veterinary Department, and Legal Department. The Army Headquarters was located in Lushun, and the commander was General Takashi Hishikari, and the chief of staff was Major General Mitsuharu Miyake.

Stationed Division The division headquarters is located in Liaoyang, and the troops are deployed in Changchun, Gongzhuling, Tieling, Shenyang, Liaoyang, Haicheng, Lushun, and other places. The division commander is Heisaburo Matsui, the commander of the 19th Brigade is Hamasaku Nakamura, and the commander of the 30th Brigade is Kinzaburo Ando. For the convenience of operational tasks and training and education, these units have all become regimental assemblies (i.e., all types of units have become regiments and reside in one place to facilitate training and increase troop strength). Also, the stationed division was originally scheduled to be replaced every two years with a division from mainland Japan. The Military Council meeting on July 1 of this year has already approved the plan for the establishment of a permanently stationed division in Manchuria, as decided by the three chiefs. This plan involves transferring one division from mainland Japan to Manchuria to serve as a permanent stationed division, and abolishing the previous system of exchanging stationed divisions every two years. The implementation of this plan is left to the three chiefs to handle. The 8th Hirosaki Division and the 9th Kanazawa Division are candidates for the transferred division. It is also said that the transportation expenses for the plan to station one division in Manchuria will be covered by the transportation expenses for the division exchange, and the recurring expenses will be covered by the recurring expenses of the stationed division in Manchuria and the division reserve unit. The implementation period is set for April of Showa 8, when the stationed divisions are exchanged. The establishment includes a headquarters for the permanent stationed division, a headquarters for the infantry brigade, and one infantry regiment. Also, there is one infantry brigade headquarters in the Liaoyang area and one infantry regiment, one infantry regiment in the Changchun area, one infantry regiment in Lushun, one cavalry regiment in Shenyang, one field artillery regiment in Gongzhuling, and one engineer battalion in Haicheng. As a result, not only will it not save military expenses, but it will also increase the number of Kwantung troops by 2,000 to 3,000.

Independent Guard Unit In September 1906 (Meiji 39), in order to guard the South Manchuria Railway, participating battalions were established for permanent stationing. Troops were deployed along the railway lines between Pulandian and Changchun, and between Shenyang and Andong, to be responsible for railway security and protecting power lines. In April 1909 (Meiji 42), the Independent Guard Unit was formed, with the headquarters located in Gongzhuling, overseeing the entire guard unit (six battalions). In June of the 5th year of the Republic of China (Taisho 5), the reserve system was abolished and replaced with the active duty system. In March of the 12th year, as a result of military downsizing, two guard battalions were withdrawn. Therefore, the railway guard unit at that time only had four battalions. On April 15 of the 4th year of Showa (1929), the peacetime organization of the army was revised, and two more battalions were added. Therefore, the current Japanese guard unit still consists of six battalions, with the headquarters still in Gongzhuling. The troops are deployed in key areas along the South Manchuria Railway outside the Kwantung Leased Territory, directly responsible for railway security. The commander of the Independent Guard Unit is Lieutenant General Ren Mori. Lushun Fortress Headquarters This fortress commander is subordinate to the Kwantung Army Headquarters and is responsible for the fortress's defense plan, managing the fortress's weapons and materials, and fortress construction and replenishment of military supplies.

Kwantung Military Police The headquarters of this unit is located in Lushun, and the detachments and dispatched teams are located in various places along the railway line (detachments in Lushun, Dalian, Liaoyang, Shenyang, Tieling, Changchun, Andong; dispatched teams in Liutiao Lake, Dashiqiao, Yingkou, Haicheng, Fushun, Kaiyuan, Sipingjie, Gongzhuling, and Lianjiangkou). They are under the command of the Army Commander and perform military police duties. They are also under the command of the Governor of Kwantung and concurrently manage all administrative and judicial police affairs.

Kwantung Army Warehouse Manages the storage, purchase, manufacture, and replenishment of rations, clothing, engineering equipment, sanitary materials, and veterinary materials required by the various units of the Japanese Army stationed in the Northeast. The warehouse was originally located in Lushun, with branch warehouses in Dalian and Tieling. In December of the 10th year of the Republic of China (Taisho 10), the warehouse was moved to Dalian, and a branch warehouse was established in Tieling. Only an office was left in Lushun.

Garrison Hospital Accommodates and treats army patients from various locations, and manages all sanitary materials. Soldiers and their families who fall ill during travel can also be accommodated and treated in this hospital. Hospitals are also located in Liutiao Lake, Dashiqiao, Haicheng, Shenyang, Gongzhuling, Changchun, Andong, and Lianjiangkou.

Garrison Prison A military prison should be established in the place where the military court is located. The Japanese army has a garrison prison in Lushun.

Defense Areas and Troop Strength The troop numbers and locations of the Japanese army stationed in the Northeast: 16th Division Headquarters (Liaoyang), 19th Brigade Headquarters (Tieling), 9th Regiment (Changchun), 19th Regiment (Tieling), 36th Brigade Headquarters (Lushun), 38th Regiment (Shenyang), 53rd Regiment (Lushun), 20th Cavalry Regiment (Gongzhuling), 22nd Artillery Regiment (Haicheng), 16th Engineer Regiment (Liaoyang), 16th Transport Battalion (Liaoyang), Independent Guard Unit Headquarters (Gongzhuling), 1st Battalion (Gongzhuling), 2nd Battalion (Shenyang), 3rd Battalion (Dashiqiao), 4th Battalion (Lianjiangkou), 5th Battalion (Sinuiju), 6th Battalion (Andong). Surveyed in January of the 20th year of the Republic of China.

Naval Defense Preparations After the Russo-Japanese War, Japan established a naval base in Lushun. On April 1 of the 3rd year of the Republic of China (Taisho 3), the naval base was abolished and replaced with a naval port department. On December 1 of the 11th year of the Republic of China (Taisho 11), the naval port department was withdrawn, leaving only a defense unit. On April 1 of the 14th year of the Republic of China (Taisho 14), the defense unit was also withdrawn. Currently, only naval officers and a radio station are stationed. Because Lushun Port belongs to the defense area of the Second Overseas Fleet, the ships of the Second Overseas Fleet are often anchored in the port.

Within the Kwantung Leased Territory, Japanese residents are subject to conscription. Men between the ages of 18 and 45 are all enlisted in the military. In case of emergency, they can be summoned and formed into an army in an instant, which is very concerning.

Important News

Nakamura Case is Urgent for Japan 64

Liaoning Provincial Government Forms a Third Investigation Team to Investigate Again; Japanese Army Ministry Sends Suzuki to Manchuria to Boost Morale

Harbin Dispatch: Rong Zhen, Chief of Staff of the Northeast Border Defense Commander's Office, who went to Peiping to seek instructions on the Nakamura disappearance case, returned to Shenyang on the 12th. Regarding the negotiation countermeasures, Wan Fulin was ordered by Zhang Xueliang to return to Shenyang and then proceed to Jinzhou to discuss with Zhang Zuoxiang. After a decision is made, it can be handed over to the responsible diplomatic envoy. However, according to information obtained by the diplomatic agencies here, the Japanese side is disregarding diplomatic protocol, abandoning diplomatic agencies, and directly negotiating with Zang Shiyi, the Chairman of the Liaoning Provincial Government. The Japanese consul in Liaoning, Mr. Hayashi, has repeatedly urged Zang by telephone to reply several times, and threatened that the Japanese army is agitated and fears that a delay in the reply will lead to major changes for which he will not be responsible. Therefore, the next steps are extremely difficult. The second investigation team dispatched by the Provincial Government's Border Defense Commander's Office and the Military Police Headquarters arrived at Wangfu Station on the 7th of this month and is still investigating. There has been no formal report to the province, so the Liaoning Provincial Government is unable to reply to the Japanese side. After Rong Zhen's return, he was again ordered by Zhang Xueliang to form a special senior investigation team, consisting of four staff officers and aides with the rank of major from the Border Defense Commander's Office, along with three company commanders from the Northeast Military Police Headquarters, to conduct a responsible investigation. They are scheduled to depart from Shenyang on the 16th. Although the Northeast authorities are making such efforts to clarify the truth, the Japanese side's pressure is increasing step by step, and it has now revealed its undisguised war preparations. The first battalion of the South Manchuria Railway Guard, led by Colonel Kiyoshi Shirogo, departed from Liaoning on the 9th of this month upon orders, touring the Hachang and Changliao lines of the South Manchuria Railway to comfort the garrison and boost morale, and to convene meetings of veterans to convey the secret orders of the Army Ministry for reporting preparations. The Army Ministry issued a secret telegram on the 8th of this month, ordering veteran groups in various parts of the Northeast to report to three locations: those in southern Manchuria to report to Liaoyang, those north of Liaoyang to report to Changchun, and those in northern Manchuria to report to Harbin. Therefore, retired Japanese soldiers in various places have been very busy these days. The Army Ministry's General Staff Headquarters has also sent General Suzuki to the Northeast to comfort overseas Japanese residents and the army, and to inspect the sites of the Russo-Japanese War. It is reported that he departed on September 12 and should arrive in the Northeast soon. Overseas Japanese residents and the army have been incited by Japanese newspapers in recent months and are already gnashing their teeth at us. After Suzuki's arrival, it will be like injecting another stimulant, leading to a clenched fist and exposed claws. (15th)

Japanese Military Demonstration Drill in Changchun 65

Territory 80 Li Outside the City Thoroughly Surveyed

Changchun Dispatch: Since the Wanbaoshan Incident, our country's officials and people have unanimously adhered to justice and actively resisted. The Japanese side, finding itself in the wrong with exhausted arguments, finally withdrew the Japanese police from Mashao Kou. When the Japanese police withdrew, Japanese residents in Changchun, Shenyang, and other places expressed disapproval, claiming it would damage the Empire's prestige and hinder development in Manchuria, as their northward invasion plan could not be realized. Since this plan did not achieve its goal, soon there was the so-called "Nakamura Sergeant Injured and Killed in the Xing'an District" propaganda. Whether this incident actually occurred will only become clear after the Shenyang side investigates. However, the recent words and actions of Japanese residents and the Japanese military in the Northeast suggest a major event is imminent. Leagues, autonomous alliances, and chambers of commerce in various places have all held meetings successively, chanting erroneous ideas such as forcefully confronting China and seizing Manchuria and Mongolia by taking advantage of the situation. Heads of Japanese military agencies stationed in Manchuria, such as Ninomiya, commander of the Kwantung Gendarmerie; Honjo, commander of the Kwantung Army; Mori, commander of the Independent Garrison Unit; and Lieutenant General Domon, all came to Changchun around the 10th of this month to discuss military affairs with Tokugawa Nakazo, commander of the 3rd Brigade stationed in Changchun, and Tashiro Shigetoku, the consul, and to inspect the new barracks built last year and the Japanese military's security situation. As a result, rumors have sprung up, saying that Japan will continue to increase troops to Changchun to guard against northern Manchuria, and that if the Nakamura incident is not satisfactorily resolved by the Japanese side, Japan will send a regiment into the Xing'an District and another two regiments to be stationed in Sipingjie and Changchun to connect with the Japanese troops entering the Xing'an District. This is because they intend to use force to subdue our country and complete Tanaka's plan to send troops into Mongolia. Their ambitions are immense, and our compatriots must not ignore them.

Since the propaganda of the so-called Nakamura Incident, Japanese troops in various parts of the Northeast have been conducting field exercises from time to time. From the 2nd of this month, the 4th Regiment of the 3rd Brigade and the Independent Garrison Unit stationed in Changchun were divided into two groups, and without notifying our local authorities in advance, they conducted a defense and attack drill of Changchun. They designated the areas northwest of the city, including Sanbu Guan, Wulibao, Xinlitun, and the areas southwest of the city, including Huangguagou, Tianjiayoufang, and Chenghoupu, as battlefields. The sound of guns and cannons was loudest on the 11th and 12th, continuing day and night. The villagers were greatly frightened, and their fields and vegetable gardens were trampled and destroyed. The damage to the Wanbaoshan waterway has not yet been compensated, and now the suburbs of the city have been ravaged again. The people of Changchun are truly the fish and meat of the Japanese. According to someone close to the Japanese military brigade headquarters, in the past two years, Japanese troops in Changchun have repeatedly conducted exercises in the countryside, and the terrain 80 li outside the city has been completely surveyed. They are particularly detailed about the areas near Erdaogou, Sandaogou, and the Chinese Eastern Railway in the north. Their ulterior motives are none other than to defend against the northern Manchuria area.

In recent years, Japanese military, government, and business people have entered eastern Mongolia and Jilin and Heilongjiang provinces under the guise of travel, numbering in the hundreds each year. They call it travel, but in reality, they are surveying the terrain and investigating resources. Those who enter Mongolia often give gifts to Mongolian youths in an attempt to establish connections. According to an employee of the Sidao Railway, more than a hundred Japanese people who are fluent in Chinese have entered Mongolia via Taonan this spring. They were only seen going north and not seen returning. It is said that most of them have disguised themselves as Chinese people and have been living in Mongolia for a long time, implementing their colonization policy. According to a Mongolian prince from the Gorlos Banner who came to Changchun last month, since this spring, many Japanese people wearing Chinese clothes and speaking Chinese have entered Mongolia. Most of them carry photographic equipment and surveying instruments to investigate and record all the details of the mountains, rivers, and resources. In March, more than ten employees of the Oriental Development Company went to the residence of Prince Qimote of the Zhelimumeng League, expressing their willingness to invest heavily and cooperate with Prince Qi in developing mineral resources and transportation in the Zhelimumeng League and other places. Prince Qi did not agree, and they left. In short, the Japanese have been coveting the land of eastern Mongolia for more than a day. Fortunately, the princes are well aware of the stakes and have not fallen into their trap. (13th)

Jiang Zuobin Arrives in Shenyang 66

Those who came with him included Secretary Ding Shaoji and several others. They stayed at the Lingge Hotel on Sanjing Road. I made a special trip to the hotel to visit. Mr. Jiang said the following, "China and Japan are as interdependent as lips and teeth, and their relationship is close. In recent years, disputes have arisen from time to time, causing various bad impressions. My most important mission in being appointed Minister to Japan this time is to

Strive to help the Japanese government resolve the Wanbaoshan and Korean incidents satisfactorily, thereby strengthening the friendly relations between the two countries. However, since I have been appointed as envoy, I will naturally adopt an open diplomatic approach. As for the rumors about the Nakamura Incident being the beginning of diplomatic negotiations, fundamentally, we are not even at that stage. A detailed investigation is currently underway, and the truth will soon come to light. I (Jiang referring to himself) will stay in Shenyang for about two or three days and then go to Korea. Recent News on the Jiangbei Dam Construction Project 68

The Breach in the Shao Dam Is Only Two Feet High

The Yiyu Taiping Dam Was Immediately Blocked After It Collapsed

There Are Rumors That Foreigners Are Contracting the Damming Project

Yangzhou Dispatch: Although the Jiangdu Duan has worked hard to rush the construction at the breach of the Shao Dam, the south entrance of Heiyutang was also completed on the 18th. Including the previous ones, a total of 17 breaches have been blocked. However, according to Dai Xingyi, the representative of the Jiangdu Flood Relief Association, who reported at the disaster relief group's joint office, the height of each blocked breach is only about two feet, only enough to stop the flow. He is worried that a strong west wind will inevitably cause it to collapse. The Central Party Department's Emergency Relief Committee has sent a letter to the Jiangdu Flood Relief Association, entrusting it to send personnel to report the damming work in detail every day. There should be some supervision in the future. There are still 4,224 refugees in the Yangzhou resettlement centers. Jiang Jifu, a member of the Dongtai Chamber of Commerce, sent another thousand refugees on five sailing boats, which arrived here and docked outside the Quekou city at Changsheng Temple, requesting resettlement. As there was no place to settle them, Ruan Lianzhong, the director of the resettlement division, prepared lunch and let them go to other places. In addition to telegraphing the general association, requesting that resettlement centers be set up near the disaster area, the Su Yi Relief Association also consulted with Overseer Zhang and agreed to telegraph the National Government, the Provincial Government, and various Shanghai relief organizations, reporting the situation and requesting financial assistance. As for the water level of the Grand Canal, on the 18th, the Jiangdu Sangu Gate reported 1 zhang and 4 chi and 7 cun. The same was true at the Yangzi Bridge. According to friends from Yizheng who came to Yangzhou on the 17th, the Taiping Dam at the end of the Yiyu dike collapsed by more than 1 zhang at 6 p.m. on the 15th. Fortunately, the salt police and local militia worked hard to rush the dam and completed the work that night, otherwise it would have been a huge disaster.

Zhenjiang Dispatch: The authorities have been collecting opinions from various parties and deliberating repeatedly on the Jiangbei military dam breach blocking project, but there are still no concrete measures. Mr. Wang Shuxiang, a member of the post-disaster reconstruction committee, stated to people when he first came to the province that the Jiangbei breach blocking project could follow the example of the Gongjiakou project in Shandong, which may be more effective. If Jiangsu Province feels a lack of talent, it may be possible to borrow talent from Shandong. However, according to widespread rumors, the Jiangbei dam breach project has been agreed upon for a construction price of more than one million yuan, to be contracted by foreign engineers. When asked to the responsible personnel of the province, they claimed that this matter was probably not true, because the statistics and surveying of the blocking work are still in progress, and there is no reason to predetermine a price and contract the whole thing. Recently, someone submitted two suggestions: 1. The use of personnel for the blocking project should combine new and old, and corrupt elements and those without specialized academic knowledge should be excluded. 2. The procedures for contracting and self-construction should be fully prepared. If contracting is not sufficient, self-construction can be prepared to avoid delaying the project. Moreover, the project must be expedited and should not be delayed at all. The provincial authorities have expressed their acceptance because they have insightful opinions.

Jiangbei Water Conservancy Officials Neglect the Investigation of Dikes 69

Gao Yihan and Hong Lanyou Return to the Capital to Report

The Supervisory Yuan previously sent supervisory committee members and counselors Gao Yihan and Hong Lanyou to investigate the flood situation in Jiangbei and whether the responsible officials had neglected the dikes. Now Gao and Hong have completed their investigation of the area along the Jiangbei Canal and returned to the capital to report a few days ago. Here is an excerpt from their report:

(Omitted above) I immediately went to the Jiangbei area to investigate. All matters related to the flood situation and relief efforts have already been reported in advance by letter and telegram. Now, the neglect of dikes by officials in charge of water conservancy in the area is presented in detail in the following sections:

(1) Custody and Expenditure of Canal Management Funds: The Canal Management Funds have always been dedicated funds from land taxes and goods taxes. The land tax began in the third year of the Republic of China. Initially, only the eight counties of Huai'an, Yancheng, Jiangdu, Gaoyou, Baoying, Taixian, Xinghua, and Dongtai were ordered to pay a water conservancy surcharge of two cents per mu. Later, the seventeen counties of Huaiyin, Funing, Lianshui, Siyang, Yizheng, Tongshan, Suqian, Pixian, Suining, Fengxian, Peixian, Xiaoxian, Dangshan, Haizhou, Shuyang, Guanyun, and Ganyu were also levied a land tax of two cents per mu. From the fifth year of the Republic of China, this land tax was allocated for the management of canals and the Yi River. The annual income was estimated to be about 400,000 yuan, but because the counties retained the funds to develop local water conservancy, very few funds were remitted. After several rectifications, the total income for the entire year of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China was more than 81,000 yuan. From January to September of the twentieth year, the income was more than 110,000 yuan. The goods tax was initiated in the fourth year of the Republic of China, and 20% was levied on the various tax bureaus in Jiangbei. It was originally set for a period of three years, but it was extended again and again, with no end in sight. It was originally expected that this goods tax could generate 340,000 to 350,000 yuan per year, but due to retention and undercollection, the amount of funds collected was very small. The total income for the entire year of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China was more than 113,000 yuan. The total income for the entire year of the nineteenth year was 110,000 yuan. This year, the customs tax was abolished, so the goods tax also ended as a result. In addition, there is a new land tax item, designating the nine counties of Huai'an, Yancheng, Funing, Jiangdu, Gaoyou, Baoying, Taixian, Dongtai, and Xinghua to add another two cents to the original canal management land tax (the original canal management land tax is hereinafter referred to as the old land tax) as funds for opening the five ports and comprehensively managing the upper and lower reaches. Since the beginning of the twelfth year of the Republic of China, it has been collected by the counties and managed jointly with local gentry. By the sixteenth year, the actual amount collected had reached 600,000 yuan, all of which had been misappropriated by the local governments. From the seventeenth year to August of the twentieth year, the funds remitted by the counties amounted to more than 110,000 yuan. From the seventeenth year, the above-mentioned old land tax and goods tax were remitted to the Jiangsu Bank in Zhenjiang in the name of the Department of Construction, and stored with the seals of the Director of the Department of Construction, the Director of the Water Conservancy Bureau, and the Director of the Canal Engineering Office, for withdrawal and use. Since March of the twentieth year, the new land tax has also followed the method of the old land tax, with the Department of Construction managing it and the Director of the Department, the Director of the Bureau, and the Director of the Office sealing and withdrawing it. Therefore, during the tenure of Sun Hongzhe as the Director of the Department of Construction, all dedicated canal management funds and port opening funds were managed by the Department of Construction and disbursed by the Water Conservancy Bureau and the Canal Engineering Office of the Department of Construction, while the county governments, county public groups, and people of the tax-paying counties had no right to interfere. According to past practice, the dedicated canal management land tax was used exclusively for canal management. During the era of the Director-General of the Canal Engineering Bureau, all the bureau's routine expenses were allocated by the national treasury and could not be used to transfer dedicated canal management funds. According to Director Sun's statement, the Water Conservancy Bureau's expenses are 10,072 yuan per month, but the Finance Department only issues 8,000 yuan per month, and even delays payments from time to time. The amount of the shortfall and arrears is disbursed from the dedicated canal management funds. This has been the case during the tenure of Wang Boling. From this, it can be seen that the people's attacks on the Director of the Department of Construction are not without reason, because the power of custody and expenditure is concentrated in the hands of the Department, and the Director of the Water Conservancy Bureau and the Director of the Engineering Office are subordinates of the Department, so how can they hold different opinions? From this point alone, the Director of the Department has hindered the independence of the dedicated canal management funds and has the suspicion of overspending and abuse. The only reason the Director of the Department canceled the New Land Tax Management Committee was that the committee refused to pay for the survey of Wangjiagang. After changing all the dedicated funds to be managed and disbursed by the Department of Construction, it was as easy as taking something from his own pocket. Therefore, since the Director of the Department took office, in addition to the remaining 114,000 yuan of the new land tax stored in the Communications Bank and the Bank of Communications in Yangzhou and Zhenjiang, the remaining 255,000 yuan transferred by the previous Director Wang and the more than 520,000 yuan collected from March of the nineteenth year to September 11 of the twentieth year, totaling a huge sum of 777,700 yuan, has been used to 767,700 yuan. As of September 11, the remaining amount was only 10,136 yuan, 7 jiao, and 6 fen. (To be continued)

Legislative Yuan Passes the Organization Law of the Maritime Administration Bureau 70

The Legislative Yuan held its 163rd meeting at 8:00 a.m. on the 19th, with 21 committee members present, including Lü Zhiyi and Ma Yinchu. Shao Yuanchong chaired the meeting. The following items were discussed: (1) The report of the Legal System Committee of this Yuan on the review and amendment of the draft Organization Law of the Maritime Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications was passed. (2) The report of the Legal System Committee of this Yuan on the review and amendment of the Provisional Law on Increased Punishment for Crimes Committed by Party Members was decided to be reviewed again.

The following is the appendix to the Organization Law of the Maritime Administration Bureau: (Article 1) The Ministry of Communications shall establish the Maritime Administration Bureau to handle maritime administration affairs. (Article 2) The Maritime Administration Bureau shall be directly under the Ministry of Communications, and its location and jurisdiction shall be determined by the Executive Yuan. (Article 3) The Maritime Administration Bureau shall have the following two sections: 1. First Section; 2. Second Section. (Article 4) The duties of the First Section of the Maritime Administration Bureau are as follows: 1. Matters relating to confidentiality and performance evaluation; 2. Matters relating to the receipt and dispatch of documents and the storage of archives; 3. Matters relating to the promulgation of laws and regulations; 4. Matters relating to the custody of seals; 5. Matters relating to the budget and final accounts and disbursements of the bureau's expenses; 6. Matters relating to the compilation of statistical reports; 7. Matters relating to general affairs of the bureau; 8. Other matters not belonging to the Second Section. (Article 5) The duties of the Second Section of the Maritime Administration Bureau are as follows: 1. Matters relating to the inspection and measurement of ships; 2. Matters relating to load line markings; 3. Matters relating to the registration of ships and the issuance of licenses; 4. Matters relating to the assessment and supervision of crew members and pilots; 5. Matters relating to shipbuilding; 6. Matters relating to the issuance of ship entry and exit inspection certificates; 7. Matters relating to the dredging of waterways; 8. Matters relating to the supervision of waterway markings. The matters in the first to sixth paragraphs of the preceding item shall be limited to ships to which the provisions of the Maritime Law apply. (Article 6) The Maritime Administration Bureau shall have one Director, who shall, upon the order of the Ministry of Communications, supervise the subordinate staff and handle the bureau's affairs. (Article 7) Each section of the Maritime Administration Bureau shall have one Section Chief, who shall, upon the order of the Director, supervise the subordinate staff and manage the affairs of each section. (Article 8) The Maritime Administration Bureau shall have four to eight technicians, who shall, upon the order of their superiors, handle technical affairs. (Article 9) The personnel in the preceding three articles shall not be appointed unless they have one of the following qualifications before the Maritime Personnel Examination is held: 1. Graduates of merchant marine or other maritime affairs specialized schools at home or abroad; 2. Graduates of shipbuilding or marine engineering at universities at home or abroad; 3. Those who have been engaged in technical affairs in maritime administration agencies for more than three years and have excellent performance. (Article 10) The Maritime Administration Bureau shall have eight to twelve staff members, who shall, upon the order of their superiors, handle the affairs of each section. (Article 11) The Director of the Maritime Administration Bureau shall be appointed through simplified or recommended appointment, the Section Chief and technicians shall be appointed through recommended or delegated appointment, and the staff members shall be appointed through delegated appointment. (Article 12) The Maritime Administration Bureau may employ clerks as appropriate for the needs of its affairs. (Article 13) The detailed rules of procedure for the Maritime Administration Bureau shall be determined by the Ministry of Communications. (Article 14) This law shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Local Dispatches

Fengxian 71

Communist Commander Captured and Sent to County for Interrogation: Ding Zhiyan, the captain of the county police team, learned that the Communist fake commander who burned and killed in Zhuangxing had sneaked back to disrupt the area. Yesterday, he led the second squad leader, Yang Xingsheng, in braving the rain to Guo's Temple in the 16th tu of the 8th district, where they captured the bandit leader. He was sent to the county for interrogation yesterday (17th). According to his confession, he is 37 years old, a farmer from this county. After joining the Communist Party in the 16th year, he was assigned as the Zhuangxing burning and killing commander in the winter of the 17th year. Later, due to strict arrests, he went out and joined the command of Taibao Ashu, helping to rob Taojia Village and Jinjia Village, etc. On the one hand, he and Tang Yixin and Li Guanjie, who have already been executed, established an agency in Kangjiaba on the border of Fengnan for secret activities. However, due to lack of funds, he has repeatedly returned to his hometown to rob the homes of Zhang Jiatang Cao Qinghe, Zhang Peisheng, Zhang Caigen, etc., and does not deny sharing the loot. Now County Magistrate Shen believes that the bandit's confession is true. In addition to sending him to the detention center, nailing him in shackles, he also telegraphed the province today for instructions so that he can be executed.

Kunshan 72

A Shocking Embezzlement of National Taxes Case: Each industry in the county of Kun has to pay national taxes every year. After paying the silver, the collection office first issues a receipt, and a grain certificate is issued in the following year, which is used to re-determine property rights. This has been a long-standing practice. After the National Government issued an order to exempt all national tax debts from the 4th to 14th years of the Republic of China, the collection officer, Hou Yiru, saw that there was an opportunity to commit fraud. He concealed the government order and completely listed all the national taxes paid by each industry over the years as debts to the people, reported them to the province for write-off, and embezzled all the funds (about more than 100,000 yuan), causing each industry to be unable to adjust the string. After Sun Boyuan, an industry member, revealed his inside story, he submitted a petition to the Finance Bureau for a thorough investigation. After Hou learned of this, he tried to find a way out and begged a lawyer to dredge all parties. As a result, he spent 10,000 yuan to settle the matter. This is a major inside story in my Kun, and the authorities are not investigating it thoroughly. It is really shocking.

Songjiang 73

Shen Longchang Accused of Kidnapping Child: Lu Zhongyu, a police officer from the 7th branch of the Fifth Warehouse, reported that a woman, Zhu Yu's, brought her child, Huixiu, and reported that her husband, Zhu Huogen, was working as a servant at Ye Sidi's house in Wu's Bridge, Fengxian. Her father-in-law, Zhu Jinkui, was cooking at Qiang Jixiang's house in Zhoujiabridge, Caojiadu, Shanghai. On the 12th of this month, she followed her father-in-law to Shanghai to work in a silk factory. Unexpectedly, she had a conversation with a stranger surnamed Lu on the ship. When the ship arrived, Ms. Zhu followed her father-in-law to take a tram with the child. When she got off the tram, the child she was holding was taken away by Mr. Lu. Ms. Zhu immediately chased after him to the South Railway Station and took a bus to Shihudang. She walked to Shen Longchang's house in the 34th tu west of Huangqiao and gave the child to Longchang's wife. She stayed for three nights. At first, she was threatened. Ms. Zhu pretended to agree. After a slight relaxation of precautions, she escaped with the child in the middle of the night on the 15th and requested legal action. After sending a police officer to summon Shen Longchang and his wife, he was not found. According to the situation, the plaintiff was also sent to the General Bureau for verification. After a false budget was passed, it was determined that Shen Longchang dared to take advantage of others' unpreparedness to snatch the child and escape, and also plotted to abduct and sell the child. His lawlessness was extreme. In addition to ordering the police station to strictly limit the time to send the defendant for investigation, the plaintiff and her daughter were first sent to the court for interrogation.

Local Gentry Telegraphed for Punishment of Seawall Committee Member: The situation of the seawall in this county is serious. Although funds have been allocated for emergency repairs, it is necessary to learn from the past and prevent future occurrences, and the blame must be assigned. Now, local gentry Geng Daochong, Wu Qianmei, Yang Xuchun, Yu Yunding, Li Zuhua, Wu Qianjun, Zheng Wen, etc., telegraphed to the Provincial Chairman, saying, "Ye Junjian, Chairman of Jiangsu Province, the Jinshan Mouth seawall in Songjiang is about to be in danger. The people of Songjiang are running around in fear and sweat, and telegrams and letters are pouring in. It is heard that Director Xue of the Jiangnan Seawall Engineering Office, at the meeting of Songjiang County, declined to conduct a site survey on the pretext of going to Shanghai on official business. After the officials and gentry present repeatedly pleaded, he finally agreed to go. The dangerous situation after the survey should be reported to the officialdom. However, the Director is a seawall specialist who has spent huge sums of money over the years with no results. Now that the danger has already appeared, the public is desperate. In addition to receiving funds to purchase materials, the Director has not yet started emergency construction. What is his intention in disregarding the lives of the people? We humbly request that you immediately order the start of construction to prevent the autumn floods. Should the Director be severely punished? We await your decision in fear."

Suzhou 74

Soldiers Causing Trouble on Horseback: Zhang Shaolun, a first-class soldier of the machine gun company of the third battalion of the second tax police regiment stationed in Suzhou, was riding the company commander's horse from the station yesterday (19th) when he arrived at Qian Wanli Bridge and could not restrain the reins. He knocked down the patrol chief of the Public Security Bureau, Xiao Zongzhi, who suffered serious injuries to his waist and other parts of his body. He was sent to the Gengsheng Hospital for treatment, but because of the severity of his injuries, his life is in danger.

Another Traveler Commits Suicide in the Dongwu Hotel: A traveler named Chen Zhongli, from Chenmu, 19 years old, came to the Dongwu Hotel outside Lumen on the 17th. He booked room number 51 and changed to room number 59 on the 18th. Yesterday (19th) at 7:00 a.m., the waiter knocked on the door but received no response. Knowing that something was wrong, he pried the door open and saw that the traveler had committed suicide by poisoning and was dying. He immediately carried the traveler to the Shuyong Hospital for treatment. When he arrived at the hospital, he had already died. He immediately reported it to the District Attorney's Office, which sent Prosecutor Qian and officials to investigate on the same day. After investigating, it was confirmed that the traveler had died of poisoning, and two suicide notes were found, one to his parents and one to his lover, Huimei. He wrote that he was a partner in the Pingjinji general store in Chenmu and committed suicide because of the bad environment.

Lake Bandits Gather to Rob Xihua: Dozens of bandit ships were found in the Taihu Lake in Guangfu on the 19th, lurking in the Ansan Yang, Chongshan, Daxiaogongshan area, fully armed and with a large number of people, claiming to rob Xihua. The district office has urgently telegraphed the county government to send a team to suppress them.

Changzhou 75

Six Lake Bandits Captured in Zhaizhai Bridge: The police branch in Zhaizhai Bridge, Wu County, learned that a large number of lake bandits had suddenly appeared in the Taiping Port area of West Lake, intending to commit illegal acts. The police officer Chen immediately led the police to the scene and saw more than ten bandit ships. He hired a civilian boat to board the ship for inspection. Unexpectedly, the bandits opened fire to demonstrate. The two sides immediately opened fire. Local people rang gongs and drums and drove rowing boats to assist in the encirclement and arrest. The bandits dispersed and fled. As a result, six bandits, including Miao Huanjin, Liu Shengming, Wan Qingda, Zhou Debao, Miao Mingrong, and Miao Rongsheng, were captured, along with two bandit ships, two guns, small knives, gunpowder, and other items, and sent to the city for interrogation on the 18th.

Nantong 76

Lüsi Dug Harbor Bandits Flee North: Maritime bandits harassing the coastal areas of Tongru, such as Lusi and Dugang, are now being jointly defended by the police and militia of various counties. Several intrusions have been repelled. On the 17th, the bandit ships reportedly fled north.

County Government Investigates and Prohibits Disaster Victims from Selling Children: Recently, there have been incidents of disaster victims in the Nantong resettlement center selling their children. The Disaster Relief Association has sent a letter to the county government to investigate. County Magistrate Zhang believes that selling children is not only against the ban but also violates humanity. He has issued a strict ban and ordered the administrators of the resettlement centers to investigate and prevent it at all times.

Salt Affairs Committee Inspects Field Police: The salt merchants in the Huainan Tong area have long had no troops stationed in the east of the Fan Dike, and it does not belong to the general area of the salt tax police, resulting in rampant bandits and salt smugglers. A petition was submitted to the Salt Affairs Department for approval to form a field police brigade in each field to maintain security. The expenses are collected from the barrel price. It has now been established, and Committee Member Zhou Pan came to Tong from Yangzhou to conduct an inspection.

Boundary Issues Between Tonghai and Haimen Counties: Recently, problems have occurred in the jurisdiction of the border between Nantong and Haimen counties. County Magistrates Zhang and Zhang jointly submitted a report to the Department of Civil Affairs on the 18th, requesting that commissioners be sent to survey and resolve the issue.

Qingjiang 77

The Lian Police Team Kills Notorious Bandits: Xu Shenjin, the leader of a bandit gang in the eighth district of eastern Lian, had been colluding with bandits from Guanyun and Funing counties for years, engaging in robbery, kidnapping, arson, and murder in the four rural areas of the county. This summer, the bandit again colluded with Liu Shouwu, Cao Dinggui, Jia Xiaoyuan, and others, bandit leaders from Funing, numbering over 300, occupying Heshang Yu in the county. They were once routed by the county police team, and the two bandit leaders, Liu Wu and Jia Xiaoyuan, drowned while trying to cross the Yellow River. However, the bandit Xu Shenjin escaped the law and fled into Funing territory. Now, Xu is secretly operating in Lian county, hiding in He Duo, gathering followers and plotting mischief. The police chief, Xue Bingyang, learned of this and led his men to search. They encountered Xu's gang, and a firefight ensued. After several hours, Xu was killed, and many firearms were seized. The matter was reported to the county yesterday.

Jingjiang 78

Another Robbery in the Western Countryside: On the night of the 13th, more than ten bandits wearing military uniforms and carrying Mauser pistols suddenly entered the home of Jiang Maosun near Bilu Market by climbing over the wall. They first entered the room of his widowed daughter-in-law, Ding, and beat her severely. Then, they went to Maosun's inner chamber, but fortunately, Maosun had heard the noise and hid. His wife, Ding, was stabbed eight times and her life is in danger. After the incident, it was discovered that more than 80 silver dollars and valuables were robbed. The bandits headed northeast after their loot.
