Japanese Army Violently Occupies Shenyang 79

The Entire Nation Should Quickly Save Itself

Stop Internal Conflicts and Unite Against External Aggression

The aggression and oppression of China by Japanese imperialists have been deeply imprinted in our minds. The negotiations on the recent Wanxian Massacre have not been settled, and the so-called Nakamura Incident was deliberately fabricated and amplified by the Japanese side. Before we knew it, news came that Japanese troops had suddenly and forcibly occupied Shenyang, as well as Changchun and Yingkou. Upon hearing the news, people from all walks of life in our city were filled with hatred for the enemy and were willing to face the national crisis. The serious expressions of various sectors are summarized as follows:

Letter to the Public from the Municipal Executive Committee: Dear compatriots, the insidious and vicious nature of Japanese imperialists will alarm and enrage anyone who can recall the various past tragedies of our country. The blood from the recent Wanbaoshan Incident and the massacre of Chinese in Korea has not yet dried, and the negotiations have not yet been completed. Today, the Japanese army is using the so-called "Nakamura Incident" to occupy Shenyang and Changchun by force. Alas, if this can be tolerated, what cannot be tolerated? Our people will die without a burial place. According to the Japanese side's propaganda, a Japanese army infantry captain named Nakamura was inspecting the interior of the three northeastern provinces when he suddenly disappeared near the Xing'an district. The Japanese then accused our country's garrison troops of killing him, fabricating a brutal murder and spreading propaganda. As a result, Japanese soldiers loudly advocated a hard-line policy towards China, demanding a military solution to all problems in Manchuria and Mongolia. The opposition Seiyukai Party even made a great fanfare, holding joint meetings and special committees, with the ambition to dominate Manchuria and Mongolia and dominate East Asia. Japanese newspapers in Shanghai and Japanese adventurers in the Northeast did their best to fabricate evidence and bribe witnesses in order to make a mountain out of a molehill and achieve their goal of sending troops to conquer our Northeast. We initially thought that this was just propaganda from a small group of Japanese adventurers and that the reality would not be so unfortunate. However, news came that the Japanese army had actually occupied our Shenyang. According to a telegram from Shenyang yesterday, Japanese troops occupied Shenyang with force at 1:00 AM (September 18th). Chinese officers and soldiers withdrew without resistance, but the arsenal was still under siege. Telegrams and trains only went as far as Huanggu Tun. This telegram has now been confirmed by all parties to be accurate. Our Shenyang is already in the hands of the Japanese, and our compatriots are being slaughtered by the Japanese. Alas, the country is about to be destroyed, and the people are suffering. How can we save ourselves? The way to save ourselves is to awaken the national spirit, unite the national strength, and use the power of the entire nation to boycott Japan economically and ask the government to recover the occupied areas with revolutionary means. Use revolutionary diplomacy to achieve the goal of compensation and apology as a prerequisite for this unfortunate incident. Then, nurture strength and gradually plan to fight with the Japanese imperialists to the death. Compatriots, the situation is urgent! The troops are at the city, and the invaders are in the heartland. The survival of the country and the life and death of the nation are at stake. Let us encourage each other. Sincerely, the Shanghai Special Municipal Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party.

Declaration of the First District Party Department: To all newspapers and compatriots across the country, please note that Japanese imperialists, with their aggressive ambitions, seek our Manchuria and Mongolia and covet our Central Plains. The corpses of Korean compatriots have not yet dried, and the bloodstains of the martyrs in Jinan are still fresh. Old humiliations and new hatreds are vividly remembered. Now, the Nakamura Incident has occurred again. It is found that Nakamura is a retired soldier who drifted to the Northeast and has long been an adventurer. Recently, he was heavily in debt and unable to repay it, so he reported himself missing to avoid payment. However, Japan took this opportunity to send troops, demolish the Beining Railway, and bombard the soldiers and civilians of Shenyang. The situation is dangerous, and the intentions are sinister. Trampling on our territory and disregarding justice, such news has broken our hearts. Thinking of the country's peril and the loss of our rivers and mountains, how can we compatriots endure this? In this critical moment of survival, we must rise up and be inspired, urgently seek resistance, overthrow the powerful, and save our country. This is our declaration.

Message to the Public from the Second District Party Department: Fellow compatriots, at one o'clock in the morning yesterday (September 19th), Japan sent troops and actually occupied our Shenyang (formerly Fengtian). Large numbers of troops entered the city and used force to surround important locations such as arsenals and the Beidaying. This action is a prelude to Japan's military occupation of Manchuria. It is rumored that they came for the Nakamura Incident, fearing that negotiations on the Nakamura Incident would be fruitless, so they occupied important places as a guarantee for negotiations. Fellow compatriots, Manchuria is our important northeastern gateway. Not to mention its other resources, wealth, land, and people, if it is occupied by Japan, it will be tantamount to invading our country. Imagine, if the skin does not exist, what will the hair cling to? Our party department is extremely indignant upon hearing this alarming news and is too pained to say more. We urge all compatriots to rise up together, prepare for this imminent national crisis, and fight to the death with Japan. Intensify the anti-Japanese work, and stop living in a drunken dream and waiting for death. (Omitted below)

In recent years, the national humiliations of May 9th and May 3rd have been deeply imprinted in our hearts, and we feel even more keenly the need to deal with the Wan Incident and the Korean Incident. What has grieved the entire country is that the Japanese authorities, seeing our people's boiling anger, fabricated various rumors under the pretext of the Nakamura Incident in order to delay negotiations. Statements from Chinese and Japanese Authorities: Our reporter specifically visited Shanghai Mayor Zhang Qun yesterday afternoon to inquire about his attitude towards dealing with the violence of the Japanese army in Shenyang. Mayor Zhang replied that regarding this matter, he had not yet received an official report from Deputy Commander Zhang in Beiping, and the truth was not clear, so it was difficult to express an opinion for the time being. However, our country has absolutely no preparations for war against Japan and has no intention of waging war. This is visible and audible to the world, but Japanese soldiers have deliberately sought quarrels and provocations for more than a day or two. Japanese Minister Shigemitsu Aoi also met with Chinese and Japanese reporters yesterday and issued a statement, saying that he was very worried about the Shenyang Incident. However, he had not yet received an official report from the Tokyo Foreign Ministry and could not freely express his opinion. If the various reports in the news telegrams were true, he believed that the situation was serious. Under the circumstances, the only way was to maintain calm and see how things developed, and then decide how to deal with them properly. He would do his best to help resolve the situation peacefully after receiving an official report from the government. Consuls from the UK and the US are also paying close attention. They all received telegrams from Shenyang yesterday, reporting the truth, but they were unable to announce it, but said that the situation was dangerous.

Statement from the Garrison Department: When a reporter from Huadong News Agency went to the Garrison Department, Adjutant-General Jiang had already gone out on official business. Deputy Adjutant Jin received him instead. According to Deputy Adjutant Jin, the Garrison Department only received a report from the secret agent in that area regarding the Japanese army occupying Liaoning Provincial City. There was no official news. This move by the Japanese clearly seeks to realize their dream of a continental policy, hoping to occupy the Eastern Provinces and then carve up Manchuria and Mongolia. In the past, our country's authorities had been tolerant of the Japanese in everything, causing those people to advance inch by inch, gradually to the point of openly occupying our country's territory, making people feel unbearable. I am a soldier and obey orders, and I love my country loyally. I feel heartbroken about this matter. As long as the central government determines the policy, I will not hesitate to go through fire and water. Deputy Adjutant Jin also said that the Garrison Department had already inquired of the central government about the truth of the matter.

Kong Xiangxi Sends a Telegram to Zhang and Li: After news of the Japanese occupation of the Eastern Provinces spread, Minister of Industry Kong Xiangxi, who was staying in Shanghai due to illness, was very indignant. When a reporter from Huadong News Agency visited him, he immediately asked the reporter about the truth of the matter. Kong also said that after receiving this news, he immediately sent two urgent telegrams, one to Deputy Commander Zhang in Beiping, inquiring about the truth of the incident, and one to Central Committee members Li Shizeng, Wu Tiecheng, and Zhang Ji, asking them to immediately telegram the Cantonese side to immediately stop sending troops and unite to face external aggression. Because at this time of urgent survival, if our country engages in internal strife again, it is tantamount to hastening its own demise. He sincerely hoped that the Cantonese generals would receive this warning, stop the war in awe, and obey the central government to unite against foreign aggression to save China.

Shanghai-Shenyang Telegraph Communication: After the Japanese army began military action the night before, the submarine telegraph lines from Shanghai to Shenyang were cut off and could not be used for reporting. However, the local Ministry of Communications' wireless telegraph was still able to communicate with the Shenyang wireless telegraph station at 8:00 AM yesterday morning. Later, due to the Japanese army's obstruction, it was not allowed to communicate, and it could not communicate from 8:30 AM. The Yingkou telegraph station was also out of communication at the same time. However, the Shanghai and Harbin telegraph stations were communicating as usual. Telegrams sent from here to various places in the three eastern provinces were all forwarded by the Harbin station or sent by special messengers.

Cessation of Northeast Goods Transportation: Yesterday afternoon, upon receiving this alert, the Hakkas temporarily stopped reporting and transporting the goods that should have been loaded. Export goods to Dalian were also watching and not loading.

Secret Meeting of the South Manchuria Railway Branch: At 12:00 PM yesterday, Japanese employees of all businesses related to the South Manchuria Railway stopped working and gathered at the Shanghai branch of the South Manchuria Railway on the 24th floor of the Bund to hold an emergency secret meeting. From 1:00 PM until late at night, they had a long secret discussion regarding the occurrence of the situation, the mission and work that the Japanese in Shanghai should bear, and various preparations for business. The meeting was very strict, and non-participants were not allowed to attend. It was heard that communication with the head office was very close.

Joint Conference of Japanese Residents: Furthermore, according to information obtained from a certain source, Japanese political, military, business, and overseas residents in Shanghai held two meetings yesterday. The first meeting was held at the Japanese Consulate General at 11:00 AM, attended by Japanese Minister Shigemitsu, Japanese Consul General Murai, Military Attaché Tasiro of the Japanese Embassy, Naval Attaché Kitaoka, Shiba Yama, Commander of the Japanese Marine Corps stationed in Shanghai, Staff Officer Yasuda, Fukushima and Okamoto of the Shanghai Municipal Council, Mirisato, Chairman of the Japanese Chamber of Commerce, Hayashidajima, Chairman of the Union of Business Associations, and Yasui, Acting Chairman of the Japanese Residents' Administrative Committee. A Committee for the Protection of Overseas Residents was then established. The committee held a meeting at the Japan Club at 2:00 PM. Both meetings were strictly guarded, and the contents were not detailed. However, it was learned that a calm attitude was temporarily adopted.

Actions of the Japanese Marine Corps: There are 400 Japanese Marines in Shanghai. According to news from the Japanese side yesterday, Marine Corps Staff Officer Tomosada said that if there were fluctuations in Shanghai due to the Fengtian Japanese soldiers occupying the event, the Marine Corps stationed in Shanghai had already discussed a plan to deploy temporarily to areas where Japanese residents live. On the one hand, it can deploy, and on the other hand, it can transfer more Japanese Marines to China. Today, an emergency meeting was held at the Consulate General, and representatives from the Marine Corps, the militia, and the various union associations, a total of 14 people, attended and discussed measures to protect the Japanese in Shanghai.

News on Reception Centers for Disaster Victims

Invitation to Various Sectors for a Tour in the Coming Days: After the relocation of disaster victims, the city's First Reception Center has completed its registration. Over a Hundred Disaster Victims Funded to Return to Hubei: One hundred and thirty-six disaster victims from Huangmei County, Hubei, had been in Shanghai for over twenty days. They were initially sheltered at the Chao Hui Villa by the Shanghai Disaster Relief Office. Now, as the floodwaters in their hometown have receded and their fields and homes urgently need repair, they earnestly requested to be sent back home. Yesterday, the office sent personnel to negotiate preferential transportation rates with Nisshin Kisen Kaisha, agreeing that the office would subsidize each person's meals at two yuan. They would be transported to Jiujiang on the Xiangyang Maru, and each disaster victim would receive an additional one yuan to cover their return journey from Xun. These funds were entrusted to the comprador of the Xiangyang Maru for distribution before arriving at Xun. Last night, the office dispatched Mr. Sun Wan'er, along with police officers, to escort them onto the ship, which was completed by 2:00 AM this morning.

Crackdown on Disaster Victims Begging Along the Streets: In recent days, a large number of disaster victims have arrived in Shanghai. Some claim to be searching for relatives and friends, refusing accommodation and causing disturbances, making it difficult to manage them. Recently, people claiming to be disaster victims have been seen begging for money on roadsides and in alleyways, making it hard to distinguish between genuine cases and impostors. It's uncertain whether they are truly unsuccessful in finding relatives and have become stranded on the streets, or if they are vagrants impersonating disaster victims to solicit money. The Disaster Relief Office is deeply dissatisfied with this situation. Yesterday, they sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau, instructing officers on duty to send anyone found begging to the reception center for verification and handling. They are also planning to establish temporary reception centers specifically for disaster victims seeking relatives and friends. The First Reception Center is currently insufficient to accommodate everyone, so an additional hundred or so rooms are being constructed nearby as the Second Reception Center. They are also considering borrowing vacant land from the Commercial Press at Song Park Road on Zhongxing Road to build a Third Reception Center.

Fujian Alumni in Shanghai Donate Clothing: Wu Renwen, a student at the University of Shanghai, previously donated several items of his own clothing. Subsequently, he gathered Fujian alumni at the school to organize a clothing donation drive, widely soliciting contributions. Yesterday, they sent over two hundred and eighty items of clothing, shoes, and socks to the office for distribution to disaster victims.

The Yancheng Flood Relief Association Appeals for Aid

To all newspaper offices: Please note that Yancheng has unfortunately suffered from continuous drought for four years. This summer, the simultaneous opening of three dams has submerged all the crops. We have been striving to protect the remaining dikes to preserve the lives of our people, but unexpectedly, the You Shao Dike has collapsed. In a moment, terrifying waves and raging currents swept away floating corpses and swallowed boats. People fled for their lives, unable to find refuge even on rooftops and treetops. Recently, the water continues to rise, and the harbors are silted up. The water depth on the plains is over ten feet, and everything outside the city has become an ocean. We have established reception centers, but the city is narrow and overcrowded, resources are scarce, and funds are depleted. The entire area is awaiting assistance. We urgently implore compatriots at home and abroad to contribute grain and funds to alleviate the hunger and suffering as soon as possible. We are in deep sorrow. The Yancheng Flood Relief Committee bows in supplication.

Local News 2 81

News from the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association

The Post-Disaster Relief Association for the Water Disaster in Yancheng, Funing, Taizhou, and Dongtai, Jiangsu, cries out: Since the collapse of the canal embankment, the water disaster has deepened in the lower reaches of various counties. The damming work is difficult to complete quickly, so we have to seek a way out of the sea ports as soon as possible. Previously, the provincial government appointed Section Chief He Haiqiao, along with Xu Ji, a technician from the Construction Department, and Councilor Zhang of the Pacification Superintendent's Office, to lead a team to Dongtai to open the Sanmao You River within the enclaves of the Dafeng and Yuhua Companies, as well as various dikes and dams that blocked the water. They arrived in Dongtai on the evening of September 6th and immediately convened a meeting to decide to first open the various Mao You Rivers and the dams that block the westward flow of water to the sea, and then open the Eight Hundred Zhang. Huang, the magistrate of Dongtai County, has written records to prove it. All of our disaster victims celebrated their rebirth upon hearing the news. Unexpectedly, after the committee members contacted the company, they suddenly reversed their previous decision, declaring that their mission in Dongtai was only to open the Eight Hundred Zhang, and they did not mention a word about the various Mao You Rivers and dams that blocked the water. On a certain day, they fabricated a telegram to the provincial government, saying that they had discussed with Dongtai Magistrate Huang and various representatives the opening of the Eight Hundred Zhang, and all the preparations could start this morning. The company's various Mao You River earth dams have been automatically opened, etc. In fact, the company had already driven piles at the mouths of the various Mao You Rivers, reducing the size of the openings, and built many hidden dams every seven and a half miles within the river, thus making the water flow unhindered, in order to deal with public orders and deceive the disaster victims. Opening the dams was just a name; it was not actually done, which only trapped the disaster victims of the five counties to death. It is understood that this time, the canal embankment was breached, and the floodwaters overflowed, flooding more than 100,000 square miles. The number of affected people reached millions, and the death of people and animals and the loss of property are countless, more than one ten-thousandth of the company's capital and occupied fields. Moreover, the land occupied by the company originally had seven Doulonggang diversion rivers: (1) Dongyang River, (2) Jiangjia Ditch, (3) Xiudejia Ditch, (4) Xiaohali Port, (6) Dagouzi, (7) Sangang, all of which were official sea ports in the past. When the western water flowed down, this was the only way to discharge water. Due to the establishment of Dafeng Company, they were privately filled up. In the face of this catastrophic disaster, even if we do not restore the above ports one by one to their old ways to fulfill the legal responsibilities, we should also ask ourselves about our conscience in terms of human sympathy and open up all the water-blocking dikes, dams, and sluices as soon as possible to try to save the situation. However, the company turned a blind eye to it, initially refused to open, and fabricated various floating words to confuse the public. On the one hand, they instigated tenants to demonstrate with weapons, which almost led to a major disaster. Later, after repeated urging by the provincial government, they clearly agreed to open, but still used means to make the opening only exist in name. The outside world did not know it, thinking that the Eight Hundred Zhang had been opened, which was enough to discharge the water. They did not know that the so-called Eight Hundred Zhang was a section of the people's land on the eastern end of the Zhongmao You River to the Dawang Port, which the company had been trying to open for many years. Now, they are working specifically from here to achieve the company's wishes. The floods in the five counties are still the same, and the company's plan is completed first, reversing the importance of things and abandoning the root and pursuing the end. What is even more strange is that the company claims that the terrain of the seaside is higher in the east than in the west. Even if the dikes and sluices are opened, it is difficult to discharge the water. If this is the case, then what is the use of all the five ports and the company's various Mao You Rivers? How can the company explain its advocacy of opening the Eight Hundred Zhang? At present, the water situation in the five counties has already spread to the sea if it is not blocked by the company's embankment. The so-called higher in the east than in the west and unable to discharge water is just a prevarication. The facts are obvious and do not need much debate. In fact, if our five counties are submerged for a long time, millions of people will become starving. May I ask if the company can be safe and sound? Thinking about it later, we will suddenly realize and understand. Recently, it was found that the important shareholders of the company are all famous people in the world. There are also people who are running around to beg for relief for the disaster in the five counties. Our people in the five counties are so grateful that they cannot distinguish between gratitude and grievances. That's why we talk so much. However, it is not easy for the company to work hard to manage this situation. It is difficult to sacrifice interests for the people of the five counties, and it is also normal for people to be difficult. If the company can resolutely and decisively open up the various Mao You Rivers and open up more breaches in all the water-blocking dikes and sluices to save our millions of dying people, the people of the five counties will be able to repay the kindness in the days to come, or reduce food and clothing, or collect food with the grain, which can also make up for its losses. This is what we want to solemnly declare. In short, the damming in the upper reaches takes time, and the relief tickets everywhere are limited. To solve the life-and-death problem of millions of people in these five counties, the only important thing now is to open up the lower reaches first. To open up the lower reaches, we must first open up the various Mao You Rivers of Dafeng and Yuhua Companies and all the dikes, sluices, and dams that block water. The situation is urgent and cannot be delayed. In addition to asking the provincial government to implement this pain immediately, we also ask all circles to support each other, advocate justice, and urge the company not to block it any longer. We are extremely grateful and weep bitterly. We hereby make this appeal.

Lake Society Speaks Out for Disaster-Stricken Villagers

The Lake Society sent a letter to Magistrate Li yesterday regarding the matter of recovering overdue taxes in the disaster-stricken area of Wuxing, requesting its immediate withdrawal. The original letter is as follows: Respectfully, we have received a letter from Fei Shulun and others, the standing committee members of the Second Branch of the Third District of the Wuxing County Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party, stating, "This autumn, continuous rain has caused a disaster, especially in our Lake area. The fields and crops have all turned into a swamp, and cries of sorrow are heard everywhere. The scene is too horrible to bear. Although various organizations, legal entities, and gentry are conducting investigations and raising funds for emergency relief, the disaster-stricken people are still worried that the benefits will be difficult to spread to everyone. Unexpectedly, before the emergency relief is released, the mobile tax collectors have come to collect overdue taxes, which is as urgent as a fire, making people even more anxious. The pumps and water wheels are naturally weak. At this time of year when the old grain is exhausted and the new grain is not yet available, it is a time when people's hearts are floating. The urging of the tax collectors is deeply feared to cause incidents. The country's grain tax has not been completed, and the order of the villages and neighborhoods has been disrupted. Your society is concerned about your hometown, so we earnestly ask you to write separate letters to withdraw the dispatched tax collectors immediately to alleviate the people's difficulties, etc." We have approved this. We have found that the area affected by this year's flood is vast. Not only have the fields and crops been submerged, and the autumn harvest is hopeless, but also the mulberry trees and shrubs have been submerged and withered. This kind of catastrophe is, as your government's previous telegram said, unable to restore the original state for three or four years. Our society has received letters and telegrams from various counties one after another, reporting the disaster situation. We have truthfully reported to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, requesting that personnel be sent to investigate the disaster area and exempt the land tax, and allocate special construction donations to repair the dikes. We have received a reply from the Zhejiang Civil Affairs Department, stating that the Zhejiang Provincial Government has forwarded your society's letter regarding flood relief. It has been transferred to the Zhejiang Relief Office to send personnel to conduct on-site inspections with the county, allocate funds for distribution, and exempt this year's land tax and allocate funds for repairing the dikes, and has issued orders to the competent departments to handle them separately. The land tax is a regular supply and should not be reduced lightly, but the disaster area is in a terrible situation. The gentry and merchants have risen to maintain it, and the officials should have compassion. At this time when the provincial constitution is sending personnel to conduct on-site inspections, it is the autumn when the suburbs set up porridge for the hungry. Checking the telegram from the party department, we find that the tax collection is still going on. We believe that Magistrate Li of your county is clean and self-disciplined and has no intention of seeking performance evaluation. We fear that the clerks are mixed and disorderly, and it is difficult to obtain cheap chickens. Or they may use the pretext of not paying the protection fee to claim to collect taxes. Even if they do not wrongly accept silk and grain, and run around, even if there are noble wines and dishes, it is difficult to hide the guilt of disturbance, causing the neighborhood to be disturbed, women and children to be frightened, and the old and weak to weep. If we handle it too hastily, it will inevitably lead to escape or banditry, which will spread and cause trouble. Approving the contents of the letter, in addition to replying to the letter, we should truthfully inform you and ask your magistrate to quickly instruct the director of tax collection to withdraw all the dispatched tax collectors and the tax collection forms that have been issued before the exemption of land tax is determined, so as to relieve the distress and avoid harassment, and also ask you to reply to us with the handling situation for record. Regarding public friendship, this is to Magistrate Li, the magistrate of Wuxing County.

Proposal for Raising Funds to Select Cattle for Plowing: Xiang Songmao and others sent a letter to the Flood Relief Association of Various Provinces, saying: We respectfully inform you that flood relief is difficult in the aftermath. The water will recede in autumn and winter, and spring plowing will begin in a blink of an eye. There is one thing that must be prepared now to avoid being unprepared at the time, and that is plowing cattle. All the plowing cattle in the disaster area are either slaughtered or sold. People in the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau told us that the city has temporarily added several cattle slaughtering sites. This is a confirmation that the number of cattle sellers has increased, and most of those slaughtered are plowing cattle. Although the government has explicitly banned it, there is nothing it can do. Not only do philanthropists feel sorry for it, but may I ask who will work next year if we sell them this year to fill our stomachs? Our association is sincerely committed to providing relief. Once the spring plowing starts, there will be no cattle at all. What can we do then? Seeds can still be purchased from other places, or even from foreign countries, but plowing cattle cannot be purchased. The dead cannot be resurrected, and the species cannot be continued. We are deeply worried and believe that the simplest way to remedy this is to select cattle that are strong and usable from each cattle slaughtering ground in Shanghai every day, purchase and keep some of them, designate rate pastures, store feed, and prevent diseases. Spread more calves. Once the spring plowing begins, distribute them to various places. Farmers who have the strength can buy them, and those who do not have the strength can be rewarded. Although it cannot completely supply the lack, it can restore a share of cultivation and preserve the life of the farmer and preserve a glimmer of hope for the society. This matter is urgent. If we do not plan now, we will not be able to provide relief at the time. We heard from the section chief of the Health Bureau that an average of 130 cattle are slaughtered every day in the entire city of Shanghai, and the price per head is 50, 60, 70 or 80 yuan. If we select 30 cattle every day, and count 1,000 cattle, it will cost about 60,000 or 70,000 yuan. Add equipment and several months of feeding and disease prevention fees, about 100,000 yuan, and we can select and raise more than 1,000 cattle. We plan to propose to our association to first draw 100,000 yuan from the relief funds, and at the same time discuss with various banks to raise a larger amount of money, select and raise more cattle, and at the same time send a letter to the Municipal Social Affairs and Health Bureaus to jointly set up a place and start implementation on a regular basis. The opportunity is urgent, and we respectfully request that you submit it to the meeting as soon as possible. We hope that you will decide to implement it immediately. We respectfully offer our opinions and wait for your public inspection. We wish you peace.

Du Yuesheng, Mu Ouchu, and Others Send a Telegram to the Provincial Government and Departments Regarding the Protection of the Embankment 82

Hairbreadth Emergency Repair Project

Speaking Out for Tens of Millions of People

Shanghai gentry Du Yuesheng, Mu Ouchu, and others, aware of the great disaster of Hankou's submergence, were particularly concerned about the recent destruction of the sea embankment in the most important areas such as Songkou. They went to inspect it separately. Because this matter is too important, it concerns the lives and property of tens of millions of people in Shanghai and the coastal counties. If a storm suddenly hits during the flood season, with the current perfunctory sea embankment project, there is a risk of imminent collapse. They also found that during the Qianlong period, the embankment of the Liuhuo Daotang Temple was washed away, and the sea tide surged, flooding the coastal towns to Wuxi and beyond, turning them all into swamps. At the end of the Ming Dynasty, Liuhuo City and Gancao Town were both washed away. The above records in the historical books are still frightening. Based on the findings of the investigation, they sent a telegram to the provincial government and departments on [day redacted], asking them to urgently order the responsible personnel to rush to repair it. People in Shanghai should urgently rise up and pay attention to it.

The Telegram is Recorded Below: Chairman Ye, Director Sun, may your administration flourish: The Shangdou Sea Embankment has been eroded by the storm tide on August 25th, and there is a great danger of not being able to protect it in the morning and evening. The public is panicked, saying that if the storm on that day had been extended for two hours, the entire Shanghai would have been submerged. Fortunately, the wind direction suddenly changed and a major disaster was avoided. However, since the sea embankment was eroded, the danger has been increasing day by day. On September 14th, people in Shanghai gathered to discuss and agreed that the situation was critical. Yong Xiang, Yue Qingyuan, and others were publicly recommended to conduct on-site inspections. On the 7th, Xiang and Yong's representative, Pan Hongding, and Shi Junwenran and Lu Junjingqing, went to Baoshan to inspect. They found that Section 5 of the Baotang Chenhua Beach, Section 4 of Zhangjiazhai, and the tail section were all precarious. Section 3 of Xuejia Beach was particularly dangerous. The lower layers of the embankment at the above locations and nearby had been eroded into countless large and small holes. People passing by were worried about the danger of falling into a trap. The seawater could rush into the gaps at any time, but the rough workers actually filled the surface to cover it up, which is deeply strange for the supervisors to fail to detect. Moreover, the road on the tail section of the Xuejia Beach embankment is only a foot wide, and people can only walk by bending over, which is particularly dangerous. It was also found that the first section of the Gu Longdun and other places did not even have speed piles. In addition, many important places had slightly placed speed piles without filling in the mud. Even in the places where construction was underway, no new stones were seen to strengthen the embankment. The newly driven speed piles were all one and a half zhang long logs, which were too short and unsuitable for defense. If one zhang and eight-foot logs were used, it would avoid debt. Regarding the engineering layer, we also inquired with the workers, who said that Director Xue only gave one yuan and one jiao per cubic foot (given by the Jiangnan Embankment Engineering Office), including all the procedures such as bagging, flattening, and picking mud. As a result, many workers were unwilling to work and left. All in all, only one-tenth or two-tenths of the dangerous parts of the emergency repair project have been completed so far. However, the person in charge of the project reported that seven-tenths or eight-tenths have been completed, which is far from the truth. In addition, the progress is slow and the measures are inconsistent, which can be seen everywhere. The Mid-Autumn Festival flood is approaching. We are doing the emergency repair project, but we lack the spirit of emergency repair. If a storm suddenly comes during the flood season, it will immediately become a major disaster like the Yangtze and Han Rivers. How can the coastal counties and Shanghai be imagined? Yong and others are in this dangerous situation and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we truthfully and painstakingly report and appeal to Chairman and Director Xue to quickly complete the emergency repair project to prevent a major disaster, and we cannot bear to wait for the lives of tens of millions of people. As for whether to send other competent personnel to cooperate in rushing to handle the emergency repair project within a limited time to avoid accidents, we respectfully await your decision. Du Yong, Mu Xiangyue, [day redacted].

The Municipal Party Department Asks to Formulate Municipal Policy Guidelines 83

Sent a Letter to the Municipal Government Yesterday for Handling

The Municipal Executive Committee sent a letter to the Municipal Government yesterday to determine the policy guidelines and forward them to the council for review, so that there would be a basis for evaluating political achievements. The original letter is excerpted as follows: Respectfully, we have received Public Letter No. 33 from the Municipal Supervisory Committee, which states, "Respectfully, we have found that the Supervisory Committees at all levels have the responsibility of auditing the policy guidelines and political achievements of the governments at the same level. Since the General Charter has clear regulations, it is our committee's duty to follow them. However, we have found that the Municipal Government has submitted municipal reports and business reports from various bureaus on a yearly and monthly basis for the political achievements part, which can be used for review. Regarding the policy guidelines item, except for the policy outline of the 17th year attached to the Municipal Government's report at the Fifth Municipal Representative Congress in May 18th, we have not seen such a policy guideline formulated and forwarded to the council in previous years. Whether the Municipal Government uses this policy outline as a substitute for the future policy guidelines, or if there is another compilation, we cannot verify it. Even in terms of this policy outline, the contents and clauses are very simple. For example, the construction of the city center area is of such importance, but it is not mentioned in the outline. Moreover, it has been several years since then, and there are many differences. It is very clear that this outline is not enough for the future policy guidelines. According to the central government's 'Explanation of Article 3 and Article 4 of the General Rules for the Supervisory Committees at All Levels to Audit the Policy Guidelines and Political Achievements of the Governments at the Same Level,' the policy guidelines set by the government should be sent to the party department for auditing at any time. When government officials change, the newly appointed officials will send the policy guidelines they have set, etc. Therefore, the policy outline of the 17th year was sent by the previous officials. The current officials should base themselves on the six-year term of political tutelage and implement the principles and policies of the party and all laws and regulations that must be implemented during the political tutelage period. They should divide them into steps and periods and formulate a precise and complete policy guideline, so that all future administrative construction can be based on this principle and progress step by step, and avoid the drawbacks of changing from time to time without any standards. This matter concerns the central government's laws and regulations. We should send a letter to your council to forward to the Municipal Government to determine a policy guideline in the shortest possible time and forward it to the council, so that there will be a basis for reviewing political achievements. We wish you public friendship, etc." We have approved this and should send a letter to you to handle it and please reply in advance for our record.

The Garrison Command Orders Liu Zhen to Surrender Within Ten Days 84

Otherwise, Arrest and Strict Punishment Will Follow

The Songhu Garrison Command announced the details of handling the case of the Shanghai Military and Political News Agency, stating: "In April of this year, the Songhu Garrison Command received a secret report stating that the Shanghai Military and Political News Agency was involved in transmitting information to the reactionary faction. Furthermore, the agency was named 'Military and Political,' implying a close relationship with military and political affairs, which could not be ignored. The command then ordered its investigation team to investigate the agency's content and instructed the postal inspection office to pay attention to checking the agency's mail. Later, the agency's president, Liu Zhen, sent a letter stating that the agency had been registered with the Shanghai Municipal Party Department. A letter was sent to the Shanghai Municipal Party Department to verify the agency's content, and the Party Department replied that the agency was engaging in deceptive practices and had been refused registration. According to the investigation report, combined with the previous information, and suspicious letters from the agency intercepted by the postal inspection office, were submitted for review and handling. The command then reported this to the Commander-in-Chief's office for instructions. Instruction No. 129 from the Chief of Staff stated that since the agency had not been registered with the Shanghai Municipal Party Department, all incoming and outgoing correspondence should be withheld. However, considering that formal troops and organizations were occasionally misled by the agency, resulting in the submission of photos, biographies, and funds, withholding all of these seemed inappropriate. The command then reported this to the Commander-in-Chief's office, requesting that the photos, biographies, and funds be returned separately, and ordered all troops and organizations not to communicate with the agency in the future to prevent deception. Instruction No. 1359 from the Chief of Staff approved this arrangement. However, last month, the command received a report from the postal inspection office stating that Liu Zhen of the Military and Political News Agency had mailed multiple printed materials from Nanjing, falsely claiming that the command had withheld the agency's correspondence and that the director of the Chief of Staff's office had been bribed by Li Jianhong. The command found that there was no such person as the director of the Chief of Staff's office and that the case had proceeded as described above. Fearing that petty individuals would use false pretenses to damage the reputation, the command transferred the entire case to the military law office for investigation and assigned personnel to go to Beijing to summon Liu Zhen for questioning. Unexpectedly, Liu Zhen fled midway, avoiding the summons, and instead sent a letter to the Chief of Staff of the command today, making threats at will. To thoroughly investigate the matter, the command has announced that Liu Zhen is required to surrender himself for questioning within ten days and provide evidence for investigation. If he continues to evade the summons, it will be considered a fabrication of facts and damage to reputation, and he will be arrested and severely punished."

The New Dutch Ambassadors to China and Japan 85

Arrived in Shanghai Together Yesterday Afternoon at 5 PM

Will Go to Beijing Tomorrow to Present Credentials to Foreign Minister Wang

The new Dutch Ambassador to China, Mr. Dubercq, and his wife, along with the new Dutch Ambassador to Japan, Mr. de Beest, and a party of seven, arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 5 PM on the Chisha Danni of the Java Mail Line, which docked at the Blue Funnel Wharf in Pudong. The Dutch Consul in Shanghai and his wife, as well as representatives from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Diao Minqian and Yang Tiyu, and reporters from the Far East News Agency, arrived at the Customs Wharf at 4:30 PM and took the company's launch to Pudong to greet them. They then transferred to the Chisha Danni to come to Shanghai, arriving at 5:40 PM. According to Mr. Dubercq, he will go to Beijing next Monday (the 21st) to visit Foreign Minister Wang and then schedule an audience with Chairman Chiang to present his credentials. The new Dutch Ambassador to Japan, Mr. de Beest, is currently staying at the Cathay Hotel on the Bund in Nanjing Road and is said to be staying in Shanghai for a few days before heading east to take up his new post.

Du Xigui Departed for Fujian Yesterday 86

Onboard the Hua'an Merchant Ship

Admiral Du Xigui, since being appointed Principal of the Mawei Naval Academy in Fujian Province by the Central Government, had been staying in Shanghai due to illness for several months. Having now recovered, he boarded the Hua'an merchant ship of the Chang'an Shipping Company yesterday (the 19th) to go to Fujian. At 9 AM, his luggage was first moved onto the ship. At 3 PM, Mr. Du, accompanied by Staff Officer Wang Xianqi, Secretary Zheng, and three or four others, arrived at the 16th Pier from his residence on Fulu Li Road by car. They boarded a naval launch to reach the Hua'an, which was docked in the middle of the river.

Local naval figures, such as Commander Chen Xunyong, personally went to the pier to welcome him. The battalion commander of the naval guard battalion, Ye Baoqi, and platoon leader Wang Wenbo led a platoon of guards to the pier for security. The ship set sail at 4:05 PM, and those who came to see him off gradually dispersed. It is estimated that they will arrive at Mawei tomorrow (the 21st).

Reasons for Shanghai County's Reassessment of Land Prices 87

The land prices in various districts of the county were assessed in the 17th year of the Republic during the tenure of former County Magistrate Lu, according to the instructions of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, and divided into three grades: 60 yuan, 90 yuan, and 150 yuan, equivalent to 100 yuan per mu. The reason for this reassessment is that the county's operating expenses have reached their limit and are insufficient for allocation. The collection of land taxes has already reached 1%, and according to regulations, it cannot be increased further, hindering the progress of undertakings. Wang Huazhao, the Director of the County Finance Bureau, considered that increasing land prices was the fairest way to supplement the land tax revenue. Upon investigating the land prices in neighboring counties, it was found that they were all higher than those in this county, which was unfair. Therefore, he drafted his opinions and submitted them to the county government, which convened a meeting of various agencies to discuss the matter. It was decided that the burden on the people should also be considered, so the land prices were changed to 170 yuan, 105 yuan, and 70 yuan per mu, equivalent to 115 yuan.

Captains Association Fighting for Navigation Rights 88

In recent years, there has been an increasing number of talented people in China's navigation industry. The Shanghai Captains Association is requesting all Chinese shipping companies to have all captains, chief officers, and second officers be Chinese nationals to regain navigation rights. Their letter is as follows: Esteemed Sirs, since the opening of trade, the navigation industry has been monopolized by foreigners for a long time. The hub of transportation, the shipping of industry and commerce, all are under the control of others, causing hardship for the people and outflow of wealth, which is simply immeasurable. In recent times, enlightened people have been calling out, contributing their assets and intellect to establish shipping companies to regain these rights. This remedial measure is not too late. As the saying goes, "To travel far, begin near; to climb high, begin low." Given the ardent patriotism of the Chinese people and their fear of a ruined nest and fragile eggs, we have been urging them to do more. Domestic industry and commerce are now relying on the shipping industry for transportation, whether to transport goods or to import goods that are needed in the country, which is of great significance. We cannot ignore the diligent efforts of the sages in China today, who are just starting their work and laying the foundation. Although the navigation industry is a specialized field of knowledge, the loss of our country's navigation rights is due to unequal treaties. It must also be said that it is because our country has long lacked specialized talent in this field, and we have had to rely on foreign talent, which has led to others taking advantage of us and created a situation of the magpie occupying the dove's nest. In recent years, many graduates from maritime academies have emerged, and their talent and expertise are sufficient to compete with foreign sailors. The organization of our association, with all its members being specialized captains who have graduated from various academies, is the highest driving art group in the Chinese navigation field. Through the long-term efforts and struggles of our colleagues, we have resisted foreign powers and broken the bad habits of Chinese people favoring the West and suppressing the Chinese. Currently, dozens of our colleagues are serving as captains, chief officers, and second officers in various companies, which is an unprecedented achievement. However, given the vastness of our country, the length of our coastline, and the fact that the shipping industry is just beginning to flourish, the need for captains in the future will be immense. Therefore, our expectations are high and our responsibilities are heavy. To regain navigation rights, our colleagues are ready to offer their services and compete with foreigners. We are not afraid to recommend ourselves. If your company needs captains, whether they are captains, chief officers, or second officers, our association can select and recommend excellent candidates. We believe that your patriotic heart will regard this matter as a crucial plan, not to be compared with those who seek personal gain. Moreover, foreign sailors are arrogant and do whatever they want, which is a deep pain for shipowners. Even if some Chinese people have a liking for scabies, they may not be so willing to sell out their country and lose their rights. Our association has spoken at length and with great sincerity. We hope that you will consider our words and instruct us. We respectfully present our opinions and look forward to hearing from you. Sincerely, The Chinese Merchant Ship Captains Association, Xu Jijie, Ji Qingrong, Chen Ganqing, Chen Jingxing, Yang Zhixiong, Huang Xiaohan, Jin Yueshi, Huang Hongqian, Ju Gong.

Reader's Correspondence

Message from Mr. Pan Xiaohong 89

In the "Reader's Correspondence" section of the fourth page of the Shen Bao on the 18th, there was a passage titled "Message from Mr. So-and-So." I felt very sympathetic after reading it because I had already had the same idea and was planning to write something to seek like-minded comrades. It is even better that this sympathetic person has come before me. Let us take advantage of this corner to gather a few like-minded sympathetic people. We plan to study horticulture, fruits, vegetables, and all kinds of crops. We hope to personally go to the nearby countryside for practical experiments, and from these experiments, we will achieve the great cause in our ideal. Therefore, those who respond must have at least the following points: 1. Have the habit of diligence, thrift, and endurance. 2. Have the idea of saving the country through agriculture. 3. Have an extreme interest in agronomy. 4. Have a firm and great ambition. 5. Have a legitimate profession and not be a vagrant. 6. Have noble character (gender is not limited). If any of the readers sympathize and think our idea is worthwhile, please write your mailing address and send it to Pan Xiaohong, C/O Gonghe Caiwen Printing Company, West Fuzhou Road, Shanghai. I will reply to each letter, exchange ideas, and conduct research. (September 18, 20th year of the Republic)

Message from Mr. Yang Jianhu 90

My experiences during the four years I have been in middle school have told me that if someone has the possibility, willingness, and perseverance to study on their own, they can certainly learn at home, and the benefits they receive can be equal to or even greater than what they can gain from studying at school. Because today's schools still rely entirely on students' ability to make progress on their own, it is futile to rely on teachers' assistance and guidance for a few hours each day. I firmly believe that this is correct. Not only that, but studying at school also wastes valuable time on courses that are mostly impractical and not related to one's interests, as well as the rigid classroom life. Therefore, I want to take advantage of the fact that I now have a foundation in all subjects to break free from the constraints of school and prepare to study at home, choosing only the subjects that interest me and are practical as textbooks. This will save a lot of time wasted on superficial schoolwork. Moreover, being at home can also give my mother constant comfort and relieve her anxiety (my parents are both in Guangdong). As for the school diploma, that is irrelevant because I see that when people go out to serve society, even university graduates inevitably end up unemployed. It is better to find opportunities to learn through experience in advance. Therefore, I have no intention of going to university. As long as one has real talent, a diploma is simply not enough to represent it and is useless. This is my humble opinion. When I have studied to a certain extent on my own, I would like to work in the customs or postal service. I haven't told my parents yet, but I don't think they will object to my plan. Before making a final decision and before telling my parents, I sincerely ask you to give me some guidance. Also, I think there must be many other scholars who have the same problem to solve. I hope you will not hesitate to use your space to answer me in your newspaper. I would be very grateful.

(Reply) Your observations are very accurate and your intentions are very sincere. We admire you very much. In view of the shortcomings of the school system and the inadequacy of diplomas to represent academic ability, you wish to choose the subjects that interest you and are practical to study at home. This will save time wasted on superficial work and give your dear mother comfort. Your plan is thorough and well-considered. We very much agree with it. However, for young people in general, there are two points worth studying: 1. If there is no place or opportunity for quiet study at home, and the person lacks the ability to self-discipline and self-study, then studying at home often leads to aimlessness and decadence, with little practical progress and systematic knowledge. 2. In addition to schoolwork, there is one thing that is not easily obtained at home, which is the development of social skills and the practice of self-governance. If the school spirit is good, this is very important from an educational point of view, especially in our country where the general public lacks the cultivation of communal living. These two points may not be a concern for you, but we should consider them when discussing this issue, otherwise we are afraid that it will mislead young people in general.

Mr. and Mrs. Lindbergh Flew Over Shanghai to Beijing Yesterday 91

Without Stopping in the City

Communicating with Radio Stations Along the Way

American aviator Colonel Lindbergh and his wife flew to China from Japan on the morning of the day before yesterday. Yesterday afternoon, they flew over Shanghai and arrived in the capital at 3:30 PM. The following is a record of Mr. Lindbergh's communications with the International Radio Station of the Shanghai Ministry of Transportation while in the air. The radio station began communicating with Lindbergh at 12:56 yesterday morning, expressing its welcome and inquiring about his progress. He replied immediately, stating, "Your station's signal is quite clear. My current location is 30 degrees 45 minutes north latitude and 121 degrees 48 minutes east longitude." At 1:23, Mr. Lindbergh asked about the weather between Shanghai and Nanjing. The radio station immediately reported the day's weather forecast from the observatory. At 1:40, Mr. Lindbergh telegraphed that he would begin communicating with XHT and XHY in Nanjing and thanked the station for its hospitality.

The Anhui Flood Relief Association Discusses Painting and Calligraphy Exhibition Yesterday 94

The Shanghai Anhui Flood Relief Association hosted the Shanghai painting and calligraphy circles at Yipinxian Restaurant yesterday afternoon at 3 PM to discuss the Ancient and Modern Painting and Calligraphy Exhibition. Attendees included Xu Jilong, Huang Binhong, Wang Jiuyou, Wu Tieshan, Shen Qianyu, Wang Yingbin, Sun Faxu, Hong Lisheng, Chen Huaisheng, Huang Zhiqin, Hong Shuan, Sun Zhongxia, Huang Bodu, Wang Caibo, Zhou Ziliang, Guan Dexin, Guan Deshang, and the association's members Xu Shiying, Guan Yunong, Li Cishan, Xu Jingren, Cao Zhigong, Li Zhenya, and dozens of others. The meeting was opened by Chairman Huang Binhong, who said, "The flood in Anhui this year is particularly severe. In addition to appealing to all sectors for relief, Anhui natives in Shanghai plan to hold a painting and calligraphy exhibition. Li Lanxuetang has already donated hundreds of genuine works by famous artists of the Tang, Song, Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties. However, the appraisal and evaluation of these works require the opinions of many experts. At the same time, we also plan to solicit works by modern masters and seek your guidance." Next, Wang Yingbin and others successively expressed their opinions. The results were decided as follows: 1. An Ancient Painting and Calligraphy Appraisal Committee will be organized, with Huang Binhong, Wang Jiuyou, Wu Tieshan, Huang Zhiqin, Sun Chunzhai, Hong Lisheng, and Xu Jilong elected as members. The committee will meet at Li's residence at 7 Datong Road at 1 PM on the 21st of this month for a joint appraisal. 2. Huang Binhong, Wang Yingbin, and Hong Lisheng will invite modern masters to Taolechun at 7 PM on the 20th of this month to discuss cooperation on painting and calligraphy matters. 3. The deadline for soliciting paintings and calligraphy will be October 10th. 4. The opening date of the exhibition will be October 15th. 5. Cao Zhigong will be responsible for publicity. The meeting adjourned at 6 PM.

A Public Bus Accident Causes Damage 96

Mooncakes Suffer

A No. 15089 public bus traveling between Jing'an Temple Road and Bazichang, at about 4:20 PM yesterday, traveling east-to-west on Nanjing Road at the intersection of Henan Road, crashed when a rickshaw suddenly appeared in front of it, obstructing its path. The driver tried to make way for it, but it was too late, and in a rush, the bus crashed into the glass on the left side of the Lihua Company's store at No. 165 Nanjing Road. The rickshaw was damaged and broken, and the public bus driver was also injured. The force of the impact was strong enough that the bus head actually touched the electric pole on the side of the road, but the driver braked in time and prevented a major disaster. The glass of the Lihua Company's window was completely shattered, and the items displayed inside were all mooncakes. It is reported that the losses were minor.

News of the Salvage of the Ship Involved in the Accident 97

The North China Daily News reported that the Haikong dredging vessel of the Shanghai Harbour Bureau, which was sunk in the Huangpu River by a German ship the other day, is now being salvaged. The ship has capsized at the bottom of the river and must first be turned over before it can be lifted. Although the construction is extremely difficult, it should be possible to turn it over within days, and it is expected that it can be completely salvaged soon. Furthermore, the Jiangyuan gunboat, which had an accident near Xiamen on the 8th of this month, has already sunk into deep water, and salvage is also very difficult, but it is expected that it can be recovered within two weeks. As for the German ship Bukelan, which ran aground on the coast of Korea on the 6th of this month, after being slightly repaired after the danger, it set sail on its own to Japan today (the 19th) and entered the Mitsui Shipyard for repairs.

Entanglements Over Love at the Ballroom 98

Fang Xueting Fined Five Dollars

Fang Xueting (also known as Fang Meisheng, nicknamed "Little Fang"), a translator in the fingerprint division of the French Concession Police Department, was recently accused of extortion and intimidation by Liu Bingheng, a graduate of the French Political and Legal University, at the Lao Zha Police Station. Detective Feng Xiushan arrested Fang at the Da Dong Ballroom at 9:30 PM the night before last. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Special Court's Criminal First Division, where presiding Judge Xu Jiashi questioned him. Lawyer Ru Bao Yi, representing the police, stated that the defendant was taking advantage of the authority of the police department, and no one dared to oppose him. He and the plaintiff, Liu Bingheng, were friends. On the 15th of this month, Liu stayed in Room 424 of the Da Zhonghua Hotel, and Fang also booked Room 430 in the same hotel. At 2 AM on the morning of the 16th, Fang ordered a tea boy to call Liu to his room and said that he had a friend who wanted to borrow 50 yuan from him, but he did not have the money on hand, so he asked Liu to lend him 50 yuan. Liu only had 10 yuan on him, so he paid that amount. Fang then ordered Liu to raise the remaining 40 yuan and give it to him the next day, and then they parted ways. Last night, Liu was dancing at the Xin Xin Ballroom when he met Fang. Fang immediately demanded the remaining 40 yuan, but Liu refused to give it. Fang then punched Liu, and they were separated by others. Liu then reported to the police, who ordered a detective to arrest him. The police are now prosecuting him for extortion and intimidation under Article 370 of the Criminal Law. However, the defendant, Fang Xueting, is a civil servant and should be severely punished for this behavior. Liu Bingheng then stated that he had been friends with the defendant for nearly a year, and the defendant had often borrowed money from him, and he was afraid of his power and dared not refuse. He has considerable power in the ballroom and is known as a "ballroom tycoon." Therefore, after he beat me at Xin Xin last night, no dancers dared to come out and testify. Today, only Sun Junsheng and Zhao Linlin came to court to testify. Sun Junsheng then stated that he was a classmate of the plaintiff and had seen the defendant beat the plaintiff, but he did not know about the extortion. Zhao Linlin then stated that she was a dancer at the Da Hu Ballroom and had seen "Little Fang" beat the plaintiff yesterday. Although she had heard about the extortion, she could not prove it for sure. The defendant denied everything and stated that Zhao Linlin and the plaintiff were very close, as everyone knew. Zhao also often went to the plaintiff's place. This time, he was falsely accused. Lawyer Fan Gang defended the defendant, stating that the case was actually caused by jealousy and that there was no evidence of extortion. He requested that the defendant be declared innocent. Finally, Prosecutor Qian Hongye said that the case of extortion could not be established. The defendant had beaten the plaintiff, so he could only be charged with violating public order. Judge Xu ruled that Fang Xueting was not guilty of the criminal charges and fined him five yuan for violating public order.

Strange Case of Two Female Corpses 99

The Deceased Were Said to Be the Concubine of a Pawnshop Owner and a Maid

Both Corpses Were Decayed and Smelly, as if They Had Been Dead for More Than a Day

Yesterday afternoon around 5 PM, two female corpses were discovered in a room on the second floor of Yichang Electrical Appliance Shop at No. 196 Dongxi Huade Road, causing a commotion among the surrounding neighbors. It was said that the deceased were a mistress and a servant. One corpse was on the bed, and the other was in the closet. They were decayed and smelled bad, as if they had been dead for more than a day. One story is that the mistress was the concubine of Zhu, the owner of the Hongyu pawnshop at the intersection of Dongxi Huade Road and Huaji Road. Zhu himself had gone to visit relatives in Wuxi with his wife a few days ago. The other deceased was a maid. There was also a child in the room, about two years old. It was said that around 5 PM yesterday, this child repeatedly knocked on the glass window along the street, which was discovered by a shop assistant across the street. Feeling strange, the shop assistant reported it to the police, who discovered the two female corpses. Both had injuries on their bodies. The third floor of No. 196 is occupied by a Russian.

Death Caused by Tram Driver 101

Penalty of Three Hundred Yuan

Bai Yufa, a Shandong native and driver No. 164 of the French Tram Company, was driving tram No. 41 on Route 1 from the Sixteen Pu to the Rue Massenet at 6:00 PM on the 29th of last month. When passing the Old North Gate Avenue on the Avenue Edward VII, Zhu Liheng, a carpenter from Tongzhou working at Dunlop Rubber, accidentally dropped a copper coin from his pocket while crossing the tracks. As he bent down to pick it up, Bai failed to stop in time and knocked Zhu down, causing a head injury. He was arrested, his number recorded, and Zhu was taken to the police station and then transferred to the Renji Hospital. Due to the severity of the injury, Zhu died the next day. The body was reported to the court, which confirmed the cause of death for burial. The defendant was escorted to the Second Special District Court by the police station. After questioning by Judge Xiong, Wang, the wife of the deceased, arrived from her hometown and appointed lawyer Wang Shizong as her representative to file a private lawsuit to seek compensation for the loss. Defendant Bai Yufa and the tram company were represented by lawyer Ba He. The defendant was ordered to post bail, and the hearing was adjourned. The private lawsuit was settled out of court. Yesterday, another summons was issued. According to the lawyer representing the deceased's family, the private lawsuit had been settled out of court, and a request was made to withdraw the case. Defendant Ba He stated that the private lawsuit had been resolved through compensation by the company. As for the public prosecution, the driver had no major negligence and requested leniency. After questioning the deceased's wife, Zhu Wang, and the defendant Bai Yufa, Judge Xiong made a judgment in court: the defendant was found guilty of causing death through negligence in the course of his work and was fined three hundred yuan, to be paid within one month. If forcibly executed and not paid in full, two yuan of the fine would be converted into one day of imprisonment. The defendant remained on his original bail.

No Stamp Duty on Da Jiali Account Books 103

Fine of Two Hundred Yuan

The account books of Da Jiali Western Restaurant on Beijing Road were not affixed with stamp duty. After a report was filed, personnel from the Shanghai Special District Stamp Duty Office, accompanied by judicial police, Chinese and foreign detectives from the police station, and others, carried a court search warrant and went to the restaurant to search it at 11:00 AM on the 12th of this month. Twenty account books were found on the spot, all without stamp duty. They were handed over to the police station for case processing. At 9:00 AM yesterday, the First Special District Court held a hearing. Judge Shen Zengshan ordered that, according to the stamp duty regulations, those who do not affix stamp duty should be fined between ten and one hundred yuan per item. Now, a lenient fine of two hundred yuan is imposed as a minor punishment.

About Four or Five Years Old

Mediation in Western Restaurant Labor Dispute 106

Terms are Resolvable, Resumption of Work Problematic

Seventy+ Unions Throughout the City Provide Assistance

After the Western restaurant industry in the city refused to reinstate the workers who went on strike, the entire industry immediately hired new workers, and business has fully recovered. The industry insists on not rehiring the striking workers, and the workers' lives are indeed worrying. The Social Bureau has repeatedly mediated, and most of the treatment conditions are resolvable. The problem of resuming work has become the most important issue in this case. Mediation will be held again tomorrow. More than seventy unions throughout the city have risen to assist. The details of the various situations are recorded as follows:

Yesterday's Mediation: At 1:00 PM yesterday, the City Social Bureau convened the Labor-Management Mediation Committee again to mediate the treatment conditions of the Western restaurant industry. Zhong Quan from the City Party Department, Lin Zhenchuan and Wu Furen from the Western Restaurant Industry Association, Wu Shenxiang and Zhao Jinghua from the Western Restaurant Workers' Union, and Qiu Peihao, a staff member of the Social Bureau, attended as chairman. After a long discussion, the first item (small accounts), the second item (extra bonus money), the fifth item (apprentices), the sixth item (dismissal), and the seventh item (Western chefs) have all been resolved. However, the third item (subsidies), the fourth item (double pay), and the issue of reinstating all the striking workers have not yet been resolved. It is scheduled to continue the mediation tomorrow at 1:00 PM.

Party and Government Instructions: Li Zuoheng, a standing director of the Western Chef Industry Union, was arrested for official business. After the court sentenced him to six months' imprisonment, the union requested bail from the Party and government agencies. Yesterday, the City Party Department issued instructions: "The presentation that comrade Li Zuoheng was framed by the capitalist's conspiracy and requesting approval for relief has been received. It has been learned that this committee has already sent a letter to the court to handle the matter with leniency. The request should not be discussed." This is the instruction. In addition, the Social Bureau issued instructions: "The presentation has been received. Since it is said that the court has already made a preliminary judgment, if there is any dissatisfaction, there is no other remedy than to appeal according to the law and await a decision. The request should not be discussed." This is the instruction.

Union Assistance: All workers in the Western restaurant industry, in order to demand improved treatment, put forward seven conditions. In view of the lack of sincerity of the capitalists to negotiate, they went on strike on their own on August 13th. For the sake of assistance, Western chef workers joined the strike. More than a month has passed, and it has not yet been resolved. More than seventy unions in the city, including the publishing, water and electricity, and cigarette industries, held discussions on assistance matters in the publishing industry union the day before yesterday. It was decided to appoint representatives such as Hou Dachun and Chen Peide to go to the Social Bureau and request that they quickly find a way to mediate.

British Public Bus Workers to Petition the City Government Tomorrow 107

Request for Relief Measures

Company Attitude is Strong

After the British Public Bus workers went on strike again, the company refused to reinstate them unconditionally, and the Social Bureau rejected the request. As a result, the workers' lives are worrying. More than seventy unions throughout the city have risen to assist. The workers have decided to petition the city government tomorrow, requesting relief and again appealing to the Chinese directors to mediate. The details of the various situations are recorded as follows:

Committee Meeting: The British Public Bus Request for Resumption of Work Committee held a meeting at 1:00 PM yesterday. Chairman Hong Mingdao reported on the process of requesting resumption of work. Then, a discussion began. It was resolved: (1) To petition the city government on the 21st, requesting relief to avoid unemployment for all workers; (2) To ask union representatives Hou Dachun and Chen Peide to go to the Social Bureau and request the revocation of instruction No. 14875 and to find a way to mediate again; (3) To appoint staff from various departments; (4) To send representatives to appeal to the Chinese directors to mediate again.

Company Strength: The British Public Bus Company, after a board of directors resolution, refused to reinstate the workers unconditionally, set a deadline for handing over uniforms, otherwise it would pursue the guarantors of each worker. More than 100 of the newly hired workers have passed the review and examination. From the day before yesterday, all the British Concession buses, except for routes 3 and 6, have fully returned to their original state. According to the company, the strike by all ticket sellers has long been resolved. The procedures are also clear. The company will not recognize any further requests for resumption of work. Therefore, the livelihood of the striking workers is indeed worrying.

Union Assistance: More than seventy unions in the city, including postal, water and electricity, publishing, cigarette, and pharmacy unions, sent Li Yongxiang, Zhao Shusheng, Lu Muqin, and others to comfort all the striking British Public Bus workers at 9:00 AM yesterday. They also proceeded to find ways to assist. All the striking workers held a welcome meeting at 10:00 AM. The representatives all gave speeches and guided all the methods to be carried out. Hong Mingdao, on behalf of all the striking workers, gave a reply.
